Promotion of National Goods Association Proves Qingsheng Ramie Scarf is National Good 107

Yesterday, a Special Letter was Sent to the Hankou National Goods Movement Association to Explain the Misunderstanding and Request Protection

The Shanghai Citizens' Promotion of National Goods Association, regarding the incident where the Qingsheng Silk Scarf Factory participated in the Hankou China National Goods Market and a dispute arose over non-national goods ramie scarves, sent a special letter to the Hankou City National Goods Movement Committee yesterday to explain the misunderstanding and request protection. The original letter is recorded below: Sirs, regarding the letter from our association member Qingsheng Silk Scarf Factory stating that the Hankou China National Goods Market was established, and our factory participated in the handkerchief department, selling silk gauze scarves and also ramie scarves. According to the representative's report, the Hankou City National Goods Movement Committee misunderstood the products, thinking they were foreign goods posing as national goods, and decided to impose penalties, etc. After reading it, we were extremely shocked. The silk gauze handkerchiefs are made by our factory. The ramie scarves were purchased from Shunli Scarf Factory at No. 110 Rongqing Lane, Jessfield Road, this city, in two batches on January 18th and April 4th, one hundred dozen small ramie scarves. In this batch of ramie scarf boxes, there were more than a dozen that were printed with words such as "Made in England Zengyu Yanghang." Because of long-term dealings and good reputation, we did not inspect them and shipped them to Hankou for sale, which led to the Hankou City National Goods Movement Committee pointing out that they were foreign goods. It was unexpected. Guo Liang went to the factory to inquire about the truth. According to Mr. Wu Wenqing, the owner of the factory, the fine yarn cloth for the ramie scarves is rarely produced in our country, so we had to purchase foreign goods for use. They are made by our Chinese people, according to the Ministry of Industry's national goods standard as seventh-class products. Also, there is no Zengyu Yanghang among British merchants. It is actually a fictitious name. Based on the facts, our factory has no suspicion of posing as national goods. However, the crime of negligence is undeniable. However, we are a small business and are in a time of commercial depression. We have suffered this innocence and are deeply pained. Therefore, we specifically clarify the facts and request your association to send personnel to conduct an on-site investigation, uphold justice, and provide relief to rescue the innocent and protect national goods. Also, according to Mr. Ding Zifu, the factory's representative in Hankou, who came to the association to report on the situation, the factory's silk scarves are indeed self-made, and they also sell ramie handkerchiefs produced by Shunli. The raw materials are indeed foreign goods, and there is no substitute for national goods. They are in accordance with the Ministry of Industry's national goods standard, seventh-class. As for the words "Made in England" and "Zengyu Yanghang" on the paper box, they are completely fictitious in order to cater to the Chinese people's fascination with foreign goods in order to increase sales and earn more petty profits. According to the facts, Shunli clearly used foreign goods to impersonate national goods, and the Qingsheng factory had no suspicion of selling foreign goods, but the negligence in inspection caused suspicion, which is difficult to absolve. Compared with intentionally posing as national goods, it should also be forgiven. Now, according to the previous situation, it was submitted to the 29th regular meeting of the 14th session of our association and resolved to send a special letter to the Hankou City National Goods Movement Association to resolve the misunderstanding and exempt it from disciplinary records. In addition to writing to the Hankou China National Goods Market to clarify the matter and order the factory to withdraw the ramie scarves from display, we are writing to inform you, hoping that your association will investigate and handle the matter, exempt the innocent from trouble, and relieve commercial difficulties. We also hope to hear from you.

Unemployed National Seafarers: Navigation Bureau Seeks Relief 108

Instructing All Shipping Companies to Give Priority to Employment; Seafarer Certifications Expiring at the End of This Month

The Shanghai Chinese Merchant Ship Officers Association stated that since China's opening to the sea, many merchant ship officers were initially hired from abroad. This was because our country lacked nautical talents and had no choice but to borrow talents from foreign countries, resulting in the loss of sovereignty and the outflow of benefits. However, in recent years, the country has spared no effort in cultivating naval talents, and the number of graduates from merchant shipping and fisheries schools, as well as those who have trained on merchant ships for many years, is considerable, enough to be assigned to various ships. Therefore, under the current circumstances, there is no need to use foreigners. For this reason, the above reasons were presented to the Ministry of Communications some time ago, requesting approval to instruct the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau that the employment of seafarers by the company should be based on certificates, and that seafarers with certificates should be given priority to employment by nationals. If so, unemployed national seafarers with certificates can be relieved, and the country's maritime rights can be gradually recovered. After the Ministry of Communications reviewed the report, it has instructed the Maritime Affairs Bureau to handle the matter. It is reported that the director of the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau has received the order and will issue a circular to all merchant ship companies today to inform them, and the third extension of the seafarer certification will also expire at the end of this month and will not be extended again.

Host Flees Mid-Banquet: Guests Suffer After Pigging Out 109

Restaurant Accountant Didn’t Know the Host; Guests Sentenced to Two Months’ Detention by the Court

Cheng Genbao and Cheng Sanbao, brothers from Nanhui, were both shoemakers. Recently, they both lost their jobs and experienced economic panic. Suddenly, they had a whimsical idea: using the excuse of their father's sixtieth birthday, they sent out invitations and held a banquet at the Danfeng Restaurant in Ximen, claiming to offer congratulations. Guests arrived one after another, opening four tables of wine and food, as well as a hall meeting for Cheng Changgen (with a fixed price of seven yuan for the performance). As the guests were enjoying themselves, Cheng Genbao and Cheng Sanbao took the opportunity to abscond with the gifts of silver dollars, disappearing without a trace. The guests turned around and found that the host had suddenly disappeared. Knowing that something was wrong, they left in a hurry without finishing their meal. Only Shi A'da (49 years old, from Nanhui) and Jin Fugen (24 years old, from Ningbo) were still gorging themselves. Shao Zaihang, the accountant of the restaurant, and Cheng Changgen hurriedly asked Shi A'da and others where the host had gone. At this point, Shi and others seemed to wake up from a dream, opening their eyes and not knowing what to say. Their awkwardness was fully revealed, and their situation made onlookers laugh. So, they called the police and had Shi A'da and Jin Fugen arrested and taken to the police station, and then transferred to the local court. Prosecutor Lei Binzhang questioned the defendants and found that they were clearly in cahoots with the escaped Cheng Genbao and others. There was no way to deny the charges, so he filed a public prosecution. In the trial a few days ago, the court recognized that the defendants were the people in charge at the scene, and although the crime was indeed excusable, Shi A'da and Jin Fugen were each sentenced to two months in prison as a warning.

Shanghai Municipal Council's New Central Police Station Completed; Yesterday, Guests from All Walks of Life Were Invited to Visit 110

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession previously considered the building of the Central Police Station on Fuzhou Road to be dilapidated, the site to be small, and the application to be insufficient. Therefore, it allocated huge funds to build an eight-story building over 100 feet high on the south side of the old site. The building covers an area of more than three mu and adopts the latest designs and equipment to provide full convenience for the police officers of the Public Concession and to seek to improve the police service. The new building was completed a month ago, and all the staff of the police department moved in on the 1st of this month. The old building on the corner of Fuzhou Road and Henan Road will be taken over by the Henan Road Fire Brigade for expansion. At 2 p.m. yesterday, in order to let Chinese and foreign people understand the internal situation of the new building, the department specially invited all sectors of this city to visit, sending out 1,500 invitations, and prepared tea and refreshments to entertain the guests. Yesterday was a Sunday, and most of the staff did not work. All departments allowed guests to visit freely and did not disperse until about 5 p.m. The Central News Agency reporter especially visited the internal situation and recorded it as follows:

General Internal Arrangement

The new Central Police Station is located between Fuzhou Road, Henan Road, and Jiangxi Road, facing north and sitting south. It is an eight-story steel-concrete building, shaped like the Chinese character "口." Cars can drive directly into the central parking square through the central gate. The ground floor along Fuzhou Road is the office of the assistant police commissioner (administrative affairs) and the vehicle affairs office. The first floor is the office of the deputy police commissioner (training armed reserve forces) and the assistant police commissioner (managing Chinese detectives and Indian detectives). The second floor is the office of the chief of District A, the chief of detectives of District A, and the assistant police commissioner (managing Japanese detectives). The third floor is the place for issuing firearm licenses, the payment office, the detective inspector of the general patrol station, and the office of the dormitory affairs office. The fourth floor is the office of the police commissioner, the assistant police commissioner, the deputy police commissioner (in charge of various district affairs, Japanese detectives, and Chinese detectives), and the deputy police commissioner (criminal affairs). The fifth floor is the office of the assistant police commissioner, as well as the fingerprint section and the criminal case file room. The sixth floor is the office of the deputy police commissioner (special affairs), the photography room, and the exhibition room. The seventh floor is the police officers' club. The eighth floor is the radio station and telephone room. The ground floor of the southern building is the police car parking area. The first floor is the armory. The second floor is the office of the Chinese and foreign detectives. The third floor and above are the dormitories for Western police officers. The ground floors of the eastern and western buildings are parking spaces. The second floor is the kitchen and dining room. The third floor and above: the eastern part is the dormitory for Chinese detectives, and the western part is the dormitory for Indian detectives. The interrogation room and detention center are located on the first floor of the southern and eastern parts, side by side.

Statistics of Chinese and Western Personnel

According to the latest statistics, there are a total of 5,123 internal and external staff members of the Public Concession Police Department, of which 485 are Westerners and 3,675 are Chinese (648 are Indians and 315 are Japanese).

Complete Equipment in All Departments

Looking at all departments, in addition to the grand scale and complete equipment, the distribution of various offices is appropriate. In terms of preserving documents and files, it is quite orderly. Important documents have a special room and are placed in more than 2,000 safes for preservation. The case files of each department are also strictly compiled and organized.

Vehicle Statistics

The police department pays great attention to statistics. For example, in terms of vehicle affairs, regarding car accident incidents, there is a daily record board in the office, recording the number of car accidents last year and this year. According to the record on the board yesterday, the total number of car accidents last year was 13,557, and last year's month was 1,172. The total number of deaths was 120, and the number of injuries was 4,462. The total number from this year to May 8 was 4,233, and this month was 175. From this year to May 8, there were 42 deaths and 1,655 injuries. The organization of driver's licenses in the office is also impressive. It is said that there are about 20,000 cars in Shanghai, of which about one-third of the compulsory driver's licenses are issued by the French Concession Police Department, and two-thirds are issued by the Public Concession. A total of more than 18,000 vehicle licenses have been issued.

Progress in Fingerprint Research

The study of fingerprints of criminal offenders has long been valued by police authorities in various countries. The Public Concession Police Department is now also catching up, and has specially assigned 8 Westerners and 18 Chinese to manage the matter. At present, the fingerprint section has retained 320,000 fingerprints. In the past few years, the average number of fingerprints was only 70 to 80 per day. In recent years, due to the economic recession, criminal cases have increased considerably, so the average number to date is more than 100 per day (the highest record was 260, during last year's rickshaw pullers' strike). If a criminal has left his fingerprints in the police station, the section can find them within two or three minutes after the re-offense, or at the latest, no more than five or six minutes. The section starts working at 6 a.m. every day, because the Special District Court must submit the fingerprints of the criminals obtained the night before for review when hearing criminal cases in the morning. According to the person in charge of the section, most of the fingerprints are from thieves and prostitutes. In recent days, there have been more prostitutes' fingerprints because of the joint efforts of the various business associations to crack down on prostitutes soliciting customers along the road. It is also said that the ratio of men to women in fingerprints is four to one, which makes people feel horrified at the large number of female criminals in Shanghai.

Confiscated Criminal Goods

The photography room and the exhibition room are also quite interesting to visitors. The photographs taken in the photography room are mostly criminals and the work of enlarging fingerprints can be completed in the shortest possible time. The exhibition room is nothing less than a museum of criminal cases, such as various unusual weapons used for assassination, counterfeit banknotes, counterfeit coins, fake pistols, smoking sets, red pills, manufacturing equipment, gambling equipment, models and bottom plates of counterfeit coins and banknotes, various pistols, rifles, and glass fake pistols, the Communist Party's red flags, and anti-imperialist propaganda slogans, etc. The strangest thing is that there is an eight-inch photograph signed by Chen Ying-shi, which is also prominently hung on the wall, but it is unknown why it is displayed here.

Wireless Station on the Roof

A wireless station is set up on the roof, with a power of 1,000 watts and a call sign of XSMP. This radio station is specially designed to assist in police affairs. If a theft occurs in a certain place, once the police station is notified by telegram, the radio station will broadcast to the police cars patrolling the roads, so that they can immediately drive to the scene of the incident and engage in the arrest or guard. The telephone room is located in the room next to the radio station, with 14 main lines and about 200 sub-machines.

Police Officers' Club

The police officers' club has a billiard room, a bar, a coffee room, and a library, as well as a small dance hall for emergency needs. The hygiene and fire protection equipment on each floor are also quite complete and thoughtful.

Accused of Damaging Debt: Huang Xianyao Should Appear in Court 112

After the collapse of the Shanghai Daily Night Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department-affiliated Gongfa Company in the winter of 1930, a considerable debt remained. Although creditors had been paid 20% of the debt through liquidation and distribution, the matter remained unresolved for many years. Recently, creditor Wang Shaozeng, represented by lawyers Xu Yannian and others, filed a private prosecution with the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court against Huang Xianyao, the son of the deceased Huang Chu-Jiu, the general manager of Gongfa Company, and Huang Xianyao's father-in-law, Zhou Songqing, accusing the father-in-law and son-in-law of damaging debt and requesting a legal investigation. Despite repeated court summons, only Zhou appeared in court, while Huang Xianyao consistently evaded appearance. It was ordered that a warrant be issued for his arrest to investigate the matter. As reported previously, the Second Special Court held a continued hearing the other day, but Huang still failed to appear. Lawyers Wu Peng and Yang Yuan appeared on his behalf, stating that Huang Xianyao was not intentionally absent, but had genuine reasons for his non-appearance. Huang Xianyao was engaged in business outside, leaving early and returning late, with his mother managing all household affairs. Therefore, he was unaware of the police summons until he saw it reported in the newspaper. They argued that the promissory note for 100,000 yuan was found in the clothing chest of Zhou Xiuying (Zhou Songqing's daughter), Huang Xianyao's wife. They noted that Zhou Songqing had been the manager of Gongfa Company and was highly trusted by Huang Xianyao's father, Huang Chu-Jiu. They requested the court to simply have Zhou Songqing verify the handwriting, and if genuine, to render a judgment accordingly, stating that Huang Xianyao was not involved, as Huang Xianyao and Zhou Songqing were bound by their family relationship, which was the reason for his inability to appear. The lawyers for the plaintiff and Zhou Songqing stated that the case could not be clarified without Huang Xianyao's appearance. If he could not be arrested, they requested that a warrant be issued for his arrest for investigation. Zhou Songqing claimed that the promissory note was not issued by a businessman, but was fabricated by the plaintiff in collusion with Huang Xianyao and others. He stated that Huang Xianyao was engaged in improper activities, associating with disreputable people, and loitering all day long, requesting strict arrest and investigation. Lawyer Wu argued that even if the money were recovered, it would not benefit the creditors, and Huang Xianyao would not gain anything from it, so there could be no collusion. Judge Shu instructed that Huang Xianyao, the debtor in the case, must be brought to court and ordered a postponement of the hearing to June 16th, while continuing the strict search for Huang Xianyao for investigation.

Famous Courtesan and Foreman: Dispute over Termination of Relationship 113

Although Both Parties Reached a Settlement - The Police Have Already Filed a Public Prosecution - The Prosecution Cannot Be Withdrawn -

Mingfang Lao Si, a famous courtesan from Suzhou, over the age of twenty, had been operating out of Huile Lane on Fuzhou Road. Because of her eloquent speech and skill in entertaining, she was appreciated by two patrons. A local man named Qin Yanqing, who worked as a foreman at the Public Works Department Transport Office, frequented the pleasure quarters and indulged in song and dance. After meeting Mingfang Lao Si, he was smitten at first sight, regarding her as a celestial being. He would spend money on wine and lavish her with gifts almost every night. Over time, feelings grew, and Qin contemplated keeping her in a gilded cage. He discussed this with Lao Si, who felt that she had been through too much and that this was not a permanent situation. Having accumulated some savings over the years, she felt that choosing a respectable man would be acceptable. Therefore, she agreed to live with Qin unconditionally. They initially resided in a certain lane on Yunnan Road and later moved to No. 19 Pingliang Village, Pingliang Road. For two years, their relationship was harmonious, and Lao Si even changed her name to Wei Gengmei, also known as Wei Heying. However, this beautiful scene did not last, and trouble suddenly arose. In recent years, Qin Yanqing not only developed addictions but also had affairs, leading to frequent abuse. Their love deteriorated, and arguments erupted. Wei felt that it was impossible to continue living in such a situation. Therefore, around 4 PM on May 20th, Wei took her clothes and jewelry and left without saying goodbye, going directly to lawyer Jin Xinmin's office. Lawyer Jin sent a letter to Qin negotiating and published a statement on behalf of Ms. Wei Gengmei, severing her relationship with Qin Yanqing. The wording of the advertisement stated, "According to Ms. Wei, she lived with Qin Yanqing two years ago, hoping for a lifelong relationship. However, he recently had affairs and, after drinking, often abused her. Recently, he sent people to monitor her actions, depriving her of her freedom. Under these circumstances, it is difficult to continue living together. Therefore, she has entrusted this lawyer to declare that, from this day forward, she is severing her family relationship with Qin Yanqing, seeking the return of Gengmei's personal belongings, and requesting payment of living expenses, etc. In addition to sending a letter to Qin, we have also filed a lawsuit with the court and are publishing this notice." However, after Wei left, Qin Yanqing reported to the Huishan Police Station that she had absconded with his money. The police filed a public prosecution and issued a summons to the First Special Court, which was delivered to lawyer Jin to be passed on. The trial was scheduled for the previous morning. However, both parties realized that it was a misunderstanding and signed a settlement agreement at lawyer Jin's office. Qin also agreed to withdraw the lawsuit from the police. Therefore, when the case was heard the previous morning, neither the plaintiff nor the defendant appeared. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, began by presenting the case, and the defendant, Wei Gengmei's, defense lawyer, Jin Xinmin, stated that the case had been settled. The presiding judge, Qi Shengchao, stated that the police had filed the prosecution under Article 337 of the Criminal Law, which was not a crime that could be withdrawn based on a complaint. Therefore, he ruled that the case would be adjourned for seven days for further hearing.

Promoting Commercial Acceptance Drafts: City Chamber of Commerce Held a Lecture Yesterday 116

Yang Yinpu, Zhang Naiqi, Xu Yongzuo, and Pan Rao Delivered Speeches - The Relationship Between Acceptance Drafts and Open Account Accounting Systems, etc.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce organized a lecture to promote commercial acceptance drafts. The second lecture was held yesterday at 9 AM in the chamber's hall. Experts Yang Yinpu, Zhang Naiqi, Xu Yongzuo, and Pan Yangyao delivered speeches. Over 300 representatives from various industries attended, and were received by chamber committee members Zheng Chengqing, Ma Shaoquan, and others. The meeting was opened by Luo Qinghua, deputy manager of the Silk Industry Bank, who stated that industry and commerce were in a severe depression, with bankruptcies and closures reported daily. The root cause was the lack of capital and tight credit, which led to falling prices and inventory accumulation, making it impossible to turn the economy around. The purpose of promoting acceptance drafts was to create payment instruments and increase the use of currency to alleviate the current state of terror. Since many people were likely still uninformed, a lecture was organized to learn from the experts. This was the second session, and they would hear speeches from Mr. Yang Yinpu, Mr. Zhang Naiqi, Mr. Xu Yongzuo, and Mr. Pan Yangyao.

Yang Yinpu Spoke on Shanghai Finance

Yang Yinpu spoke on the relationship between acceptance drafts and Shanghai finance. The outline was as follows: (1) The Meaning of Finance: A. Supply of Funds (lenders), B. Demand for Funds (due to lack of working capital in industry and commerce) (borrowers), C. Regulation of Funds: Financial institutions, where those with capital and financial institutions use each other to promote prosperity, and neither should be neglected. (2) The Current Situation of Shanghai Finance: A. The Root of Financial Problems: a. Cause: The impact of the U.S. silver policy, b. Root cause: The lack of a sound financial market, B. The Current Situation of Financial Tightness: Currency contraction, a. Legal tender contraction: The result of cash exports, b. Paper money contraction: Due to the decrease in cash, paper money cannot be issued, c. Credit contraction: Reduction in loans, real estate stagnation, C. The Impact of Currency Contraction: a. Domestically, prices fall and industry and commerce are depressed, b. Externally, foreign exchange rates rise and exports are hindered. (3) Acceptance Drafts and Shanghai Finance: A. Temporary Function: To increase the number of safe and liquid credit instruments on the market, increase the amount of capital on the market, and improve the current currency contraction phenomenon, B. Permanent Impact: a. Change the nature of borrowing and lending in the market, b. Create a key to control the market. (4) Conclusion: A. The common circulation of acceptance drafts can improve the phenomenon of currency contraction, B. The common circulation of acceptance drafts can increase the security of Shanghai finance, which is sufficient to encourage the supply of funds (benefiting depositors), and on the other hand, increase the liquidity of Shanghai finance, which is sufficient to regulate the demand for funds (benefiting those lacking capital). This is not only beneficial to the financial industry's own capital utilization, C. The implementation of rediscounting can increase the liquidity of general bank funds on the one hand, and increase the central bank's control over the market on the other. The financial organization itself will gradually become stable and will be able to assist industry and commerce as much as possible, as a legitimate means of development.

Zhang Naiqi Spoke on the Open Account System

Zhang Naiqi spoke on the relationship between acceptance drafts and the old open account system. The outline was as follows: (1) The Reasons for the Staleness of Industrial and Commercial Assets: A. Too much fixed assets and equipment costs, B. Too much inventory, C. Too many open accounts, the most important factor. (2) Commercial Acceptance Drafts Can Solve the Most Important Stagnant Factors: A. Converting book debt into documented rights, B. Turning documented rights into cash through rediscounting methods. (3) Commercial Acceptance Drafts Can Reduce Commodity Costs: a. Flexible capital turnover allows for more buying and selling, thereby reducing the burden of expenses, b. Financial institutions are willing to rediscount drafts at lower interest rates, also reducing the burden of interest. c. Reduced factory costs allow merchants to obtain cheaper goods, so promoting commercial acceptance drafts is beneficial to oneself. (4) The Reasons for Financial Institutions' Staleness of Assets: A. Too much real estate, B. Stagnant loans, one of the most important factors. (5) Analysis of Financial Institutions' Stagnant Loans: A. Unmatured book debt cannot be freely transferred to others to obtain financing, B. Matured loans cannot be repaid on time. (6) Rediscounting Drafts Can Solve the Stagnation of Loans: A. Rediscounted drafts are documented rights that can be transferred to the national bank through rediscounting methods to obtain financing, B. Rediscounted drafts are often transferred, and draft debtors, in order to maintain their credit, will not delay payment, C. Therefore, financial institutions are willing to rediscount drafts at lower interest rates.

Xu Yongzuo Spoke on the Accounting System

Xu Yongzuo spoke on the relationship between commercial acceptance drafts and accounting. The purpose of accounting is to accurately and clearly determine the value of assets, and their value lies in increasing liquidity. I am very pleased with the promotion of acceptance drafts. Please allow me to briefly explain. (1) The Accuracy of Commercial Acceptance Drafts and Accounting: Accounting values accuracy, and the promotion of commercial acceptance drafts will make accounting more accurate. Commercial acceptance drafts have a definite term, detailed records, and a definite amount. (a) The term of commercial open accounts can be determined, (b) The evidence of open accounts can be reliable, (c) The amount of open accounts can be accurate, and (d) Financial seasons can be adjusted without causing panic, and (e) Fraud can be prevented and disputes avoided. (2) Commercial Acceptance Drafts and Asset Liquidity: The first priority of asset organization is to seek a thick net asset. However, a thick net asset lacking liquidity is still not good for operation. Now, promoting commercial acceptance drafts can increase the liquidity of assets. Commercial acceptance drafts have turned book debt into documented debt, which can be transferred, rediscounted, and turned into cash, which helps increase the turnover rate of funds. (3) Points to Note in Accounting for the Use of Commercial Acceptance Drafts: Merchants in our country have historically been very negligent in recording drafts, often mixing them with business transactions and rolling cash. Now, with the promotion of commercial acceptance drafts, the recording of drafts cannot be as simple as before. The main book should have records of incoming drafts (i.e., accounts receivable) and outgoing drafts (i.e., accounts payable). The subsidiary book should have detailed records of the incoming draft book (or the incoming draft entry book) and the outgoing draft book (or the payment draft entry book), and there should also be additional records of potential debts and collection rights for endorsement transfers.

Pan Yangyao Spoke on Industrial and Commercial Self-Help

Pan Yangyao spoke on commercial acceptance drafts and industry and commerce. The main points were: (1) The current difficulties of industry and commerce are nothing more than the following: (1) Market shrinkage, (2) Heavy taxes, (3) Labor disputes, (4) Difficult collection of accounts, (5) Shortage of funds. Among these, items (1), (4), and (5) are particularly important to the survival of industry and commerce. Analyzing them further, items (1) and (4) are the causes, and item (5) is the result. Looking at the factories and stores that have closed down recently, they all had poor turnover, accumulated inventory, and excessive accounts, which were fatal blows. Last year, the United States implemented the Silver Purchase Act, and China's silver surplus reached 260 million yuan. Currency contraction caused banks to reduce loans and increase reserves as a means of preventing panic. Therefore, the bank loans that usually sustained industry and commerce suddenly became scarce, plunging them into the abyss of panic. (2) The biggest reason for the shortage of funds in industry and commerce is that our country's open account system cannot adapt to the needs of the new economic world, causing most of the funds to become stagnant book debt. (3) Promoting commercial acceptance drafts is sufficient to mobilize commercial funds. The simplest method is to try to turn the vacant book debt into circulating draft debt. The only way is to promote commercial acceptance drafts, because acceptance drafts are issued by the seller and sent to the buyer or its agent bank for acceptance. If the seller needs funds temporarily, it can apply to the bank for rediscounting, collect cash, or transfer it to others to replace cash. This kind of rolling circulation is equivalent to increasing the amount of capital on the market. (4) The benefits of promoting commercial acceptance drafts: Since the contraction policy of our country's financial sector is so severe and the need for funds in industry and commerce is so urgent, in this acute contradictory situation, industry and commerce can only try to solve this difficulty through their own efforts. Therefore, promoting commercial acceptance drafts is an effective tool for self-help in industry and commerce. Economists, financiers, and government authorities have jointly advocated for acceptance drafts, hoping that industry and commerce can honestly implement them to adapt to the needs of this era. If they can be promoted to the fullest extent, then in Shanghai alone, the daily transactions will be no less than tens of millions of yuan. The acceptance drafts issued based on this business can supply society with tens of millions of yuan of capital. We should still remember that during January and February of this year, industry and commerce suffered a great shortage of funds. Therefore, organizations such as the Industrial and Commercial Relief Alliance were formed to jointly appeal to the government and society, requesting the financial sector to continue lending as usual. After several months of fuss, a credit loan of 5 million yuan was reluctantly approved for consideration. Until now, there has been no news of any disbursement. It can be seen that in all difficulties, waiting for external relief is always difficult and unprofitable. It is better to ask for help from oneself than from others. If industry and commerce can make a great determination to improve themselves, starting with their own improvements, and first try to circulate tens of millions of yuan of book debt on the market, and strengthen the credit of acceptance drafts with human effort, then the financial sector may change its previous stingy attitude towards rediscounting loans, vying for fear of being too late. On this point, I can say with certainty that in any difficult situation, one must first devise countermeasures. If the progress is smooth, then one can hope for external assistance. Promoting acceptance drafts is a good way for industry and commerce to solve their own difficulties.

Russian Community: Yesterday Commemorated the Centenary of Pushkin 118

The White Russian Club Held a Meeting, Lecture, and Banquet - The Youth Literary Association Held a Commemoration in the Afternoon

According to Shen Shi News Agency, June 9th is a cultural memorial day for old Russia, and also the birth anniversary of the deceased old Russian writer and world-renowned national poet Pushkin. Pushkin was born on January 29th, and this year marks the centenary of his birth. To show their solemn respect, the Russians postponed Pushkin's birthday by one day and combined it with the cultural commemoration yesterday. The details are as follows:

Grand Celebration in the Club

Yesterday at 9 PM, the White Russians gathered at No. 746 Fuxu Road to hold a grand celebration banquet. First, the choir led by Massisiss sang the old Russian national anthem. Next, Bishop John of the White Russian Orthodox Church gave a lecture on "The Influence of Russian Culture on the Church." Then, Savetolov lectured on the history of Pushkin. There were also solo and choral performances in between. Finally, the choir sang a Pushkin commemorative song and the event ended.

Youth Literary Association Held a Meeting to Commemorate

The Russian Youth Literary Association held a commemorative meeting at 5 PM yesterday at the Russian Sports Association at No. 883 Weihaiwei Road. The meeting included a lecture by Mr. John, and several Russian representatives reported on Russian culture, history, music, cultural activities, and their contributions to the world. After the lecture, several famous old Russian actors and actresses performed a drama, and a band composed of famous Russian musicians participated in the performance. Finally, everyone sang the old Russian national anthem and the event ended.

Ms. Huang Xinmian dedicated herself to the women's movement for many years, founding "Women's Bookstore," "Women's Monthly," and "Women's Library," among others, which exhausted her physically and mentally. She passed away on May 4th at the Women and Children's Hospital. Yesterday at 2:00 PM, ten groups from Nanjing and Shanghai held a memorial service at Jue Lin Temple on Avenue Joffre. At that time, Avenue Joffre was bustling with traffic and a large crowd had gathered. The ceremony began with Master of Ceremonies Mr. Sun Hengge announcing the commencement of the service. Mr. Sun Hengge, representing Fudan University and the Jiangxi Alumni Association, delivered a speech, stating that Ms. Huang's death in the troubled month of May made her even more mourned. Her death on the anniversary of the May Fourth Movement, a time of cultural movement revival and intense women's movement activity, made it all the more regrettable that Ms. Huang, who held a leading position in the women's movement, had passed away. In closing, he hoped that Mr. Yao and members of society could complete Ms. Huang's unfinished work in the women's movement. Finally, Ms. Zhao Qingge of the Women's Bookstore delivered a speech, briefly stating that she would resolutely strive to complete Ms. Huang's work in the future. The family representative, Mr. Yao Mingda, then delivered a response, his voice hoarse before he even spoke, tears streaming down his face, his grief overwhelming. He spoke of three points: (1) Gratitude; (2) Repentance; (3) Continuing Ms. Huang's legacy and striving forward. The audience was deeply moved and unable to look up. In the end, a photograph was taken, the ceremony concluded, and the funeral procession departed at 4:00 PM for burial at the Xujiahui Xuchang Bridge Jiangxi Public Cemetery.

Young Man Lacks Courage, Commits Suicide Due to Economic Pressure 129

Cao Chengduo, a 24-year-old youth from Ningbo, came to Shanghai from his native Ningbo to do business some years ago. Recently, due to the impact of the economic downturn, he became unemployed. Although he asked relatives and friends to help him find a job, he was ultimately unsuccessful. Having been unemployed for a long time, he tasted much suffering. Furthermore, he had no money, no place to stay, and drifted on the streets. He then conceived the idea of ​​ending his life. The day before yesterday, he went to room 309 of the Ningbo Merchants Hotel on Tianjin Road in the Public Concession, where he secretly ingested raw opium and went to bed. It was not until about 12:00 PM yesterday that a waiter discovered him and immediately reported it to the front desk, who in turn telephoned the relevant police station. Detectives were dispatched to investigate, and Cao was quickly sent to Renji Hospital for emergency treatment. Doctors diagnosed that he had indeed ingested opium, but the poisoning was too severe and there was no way to save him. He died shortly thereafter.

Record of the Case of Robbing a Coffin Lid and Extorting Money 130

Song, the daughter-in-law of Chen Fengchun, a villager residing at No. 47 Nancaojiazhai, Caojiadu, West Shanghai, passed away from illness a few days ago. The next day (May 31st), the coffin was prepared for burial. However, members of the same clan, Chen Taosheng, Chen Qingzhang, and others, gathered a crowd to seize the coffin lid and hide it in the Yongkang Lane in the back. Chen Fengchun's wife, Chen Li, reported this to the police station, which dispatched officers to recover the coffin lid and arrest the Shandong men Zhu Xiaodi, Zhao Xinnian, Zhang Xianming, Zhao Baoshan, as well as Chen Taosheng and Chen Qingzhang, a total of six people, who were taken to the Caojiadu Police Station for interrogation and detention. It is now known that the cause of this incident stems from the fact that Chen Fengchun (60 years old this year) had only one son, Gou Di, who died six years ago. He married Zhu (the deceased) and had a granddaughter, Zhaodi, who is eleven years old this year, and a grandson, Longlong, who died at the age of five. Chen Fengchun was saddened by the death of his son and grandson, and in order to ensure the continuation of his lineage, he consulted with his wife, Chen Li (61 years old), two years ago and obtained her consent to take Fan (32 years old) as a concubine. Last year, she gave birth to a daughter, named Miaodi. Chen Fengchun owns a house and several acres of land, from which he can collect over a thousand yuan in rent each year, allowing him to live comfortably. This time, when his daughter-in-law Song passed away from dysentery, his cousin Chen Taosheng, his grand-nephew Chen Qingzhang, and others came forward to obstruct the [unclear] collection and extort two thousand gold coins without success. Therefore, they seized the coffin lid and instructed the Shandong strongmen Zhu Xiaodi, and others to guard it. At the time when the police arrested Zhu and others, they confiscated four iron bars (weapons prepared for resistance) and sent them to the local court for interrogation and detention along with the others. Yesterday afternoon, Prosecutor Wu Deying summoned Chen Li to the court for investigation. She recounted the previous events in detail. He then ordered the detained Chen Taosheng, Chen Qingzhang, and others to be interrogated strictly for a long time and ordered them to be returned to custody for further investigation.

Municipal Federation Requests Landlords in the 21st District to Reduce Rent 131

The 21st District Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Federation of Citizens sent a letter yesterday to the property companies on Hankou and Shanxi Roads, stating: (Omitted above) This District of the Federation is located on Hankou and Shanxi Roads, a district known for its flourishing commerce. Since the January 28th Incident, the market has been in decline, and recently, shops have been closing down every day. The market is deserted, and travelers are reluctant to come. The reason for this is due to the slow business and the high rent, making it impossible to sustain operations. If this continues, the shops on these two roads will likely become mostly vacant. This Federation has received numerous letters from its members, stating that the social situation is not good and requesting that we find a way to provide relief. After deliberation, we believe that the prosperity or decline of businesses on these two roads is closely related to the issue of rent. If rent is low, shop owners will naturally try their best to maintain their businesses. If rent is high and business is slow, shop owners will be unable to maintain their businesses, resulting in rent arrears and closures. However, landlords will also suffer losses as a result. Although a small number of tenants are currently maintaining their businesses, they will eventually fail. We propose that landlords consider the social situation and, instead of leaving their properties vacant, consider reducing rent appropriately to prevent vacancies. This would allow shops to be lined up, and the market might recover as a result. Although landlords may lose a small amount of rent, they will avoid the loss of having vacant properties. The Company's properties are numerous within this Federation's District, and the number of vacant properties is also not small. Although the loss of rent may not be significant for the Company, the social situation should be addressed to help maintain the market and restore its past prosperity. These are the views of the members of this Federation, and we respectfully submit them for your consideration and adoption. (Omitted below)

The National Painting Monthly, published by the Chinese Painting Association and edited by He Dajian, the executive director of the association, has been increasing in sales since its publication, because the magazine is orthodox and the material is carefully selected. The seventh issue has now been published, containing articles by Xia Jingguan, Huang Binhong, Shi Chongpeng, Yu Jianhua, He Tianjian, and others. Xia's "Rise and Fall of Imperial Painting Academies Through the Dynasties" is a valuable textual research article. Shi's "Paintings in the London Chinese Art Exhibition" details the dimensions, inscriptions, brushwork, and ink of each painting, as well as biographies of the artists. Those who have not seen the pre-exhibition will feel as if they are there by reading this. Huang's "On Painting, One Should Take What Is Good" is the most insightful discourse. Illustrations include long scrolls by Zhou Lecun, Dong Qichang, Lu Hong, Song Shancao Zhang Tu, Bada Shanren, Wang Ai, and other famous works. The delay in the publication of this issue is said to be due to improvements in editing. It is published monthly, one issue per month, and retails for one silver dollar per issue. The annual subscription for twelve issues, including postage, is one yuan and two jiao. General sales agents: Hanwen Zhengkai Printing Bureau on Shandong Road, Shanghai; Tianjin Dagongbao Shanghai Branch on Second Road, Shanghai. Editorial office: No. [unclear], Xihu Lane, Ximen Road, Shanghai.

Emergency Meeting of Rent Reduction Association in Yuqing Lane, Tianliu Road 136

Due to the economic downturn, the Rent Reduction Committee of Yuqing Lane, Laotangjia Lane, Datong Road in this city, previously sent a public letter to the landlord Zheng Zuoji on the 30th of last month, jointly signed and stamped by all the tenants of the lane, requesting a reduction in rent. This was reported in the previous issue. However, not only has there been no indication of rent reduction to date, but the landlord has also used high-pressure tactics, using the law as a shield, and filed a complaint with the First Court of the Special District on the 5th, suing six tenants of the lane: Wang Jinfeng, Shi Genjin, Ruitaiyuan, Li Jiaxiang, Gu Zhongzu, and Cao Zhenfan. After receiving the summons, the tenants reported to the association. After deliberation by the executive committee, it was decided that since the landlord disregarded the facts and the market situation, ignored the rent reduction issue, and instead sought to increase profits, using litigation as a weapon, the executive committee had no choice but to convene a temporary emergency meeting at the association's office in Lane 4 yesterday (9th) at 4:00 PM to discuss countermeasures. Over fifty tenants signed in and elected Yu Tingyang as chairman to preside over the meeting. The formalities were carried out, and the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and the progress of the rent reduction request. The lawyers Yu Chuanding and Zhang [unclear] were hired as legal advisors to handle legal matters. It was unanimously resolved that all rent in the lane would be deposited by the tenants and the rent reduction association in the Postal Savings Bureau. Rent would not be paid until the goal of rent reduction was achieved. The Rent Reduction General Association would also be notified and requested to provide assistance.

Free Talk

Arresting Souls to Support Bridge Piers 141

— Cao Juren

Recently, it was reported that villagers in Shaoxing gathered a crowd of over a thousand to destroy the home of a certain Zhou, claiming that Zhou had organized a "Tongshan Society" to secretly investigate villagers' names, ages, and birthdates. Those investigated would have their souls captured to support the bridge piers of the Qian Tang River Bridge, which was then under construction. Why iron bridge piers necessarily require souls to support them, I truly don't understand. However, in my mere thirty-plus years of life, I've seen this kind of thing countless times. In the summer of the third year of the Republic of China (1914), a major disturbance erupted in the Zhe Dong area, known as the "School-Age Children Uprising." That spring, each county had been ordered to investigate school-age children. After midsummer, there was a drought everywhere, with no rain for three consecutive months, resulting in a very poor harvest. Coincidentally, in early autumn, World War I broke out, and Germans rushed back to their country. The construction of the iron bridge over the Caoe River suddenly stopped. Rumors then spread, saying that even the foreign devils were helpless with that iron bridge and needed to capture the souls of children to support the bridge piers. All the children who had been investigated in the spring were on the list to be captured. Thus, a major disturbance erupted, with attacks on schools, killings of investigators, burning of county offices, and the appearance of so-called "Infant Loving Armies." In families, there were even more tricks, including hiring Taoist priests, smearing dog blood, wearing seven-star coins, finding Hongwu Tongbao coins, and hanging fragrant sachets—everything imaginable. Following this came the government's busyness, sending troops, executing people, beheading people, posting announcements, and sending propagandists. Eventually, things disappeared without a trace and became quiet. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China (1929), when the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum in Nanjing was under construction, Nanjing was filled with rumors of capturing souls to build the mausoleum. Children were again covered in yellow bags and seven-star coins. In the nineteenth year of the Republic of China (1930), there were rumors again in the Tai Lake area of capturing the souls of elementary school students to support bridge piers. Elementary schools in the Jiaxing and Huzhou area even had all students taking leave to return home. This time, the rumor in Shaoxing of capturing souls to support bridge piers is nothing more than a rerun of an old play, with different roles and locations. The origin of this kind of legend is very ancient. In the twenty-seventh year of the Kaiyuan era of the Tang Emperor Xuanzong, the Mingtang was rebuilt. Rumors spread that "officials are taking young children and burying them beneath the Mingtang to suppress evil. Children in villages and fields are hidden in valleys; the capital city is in turmoil." This shows that the legend from 1300 years ago is exactly the same as the current legend. Earlier legends than Kaiyuan include the legend of the Sui Emperor Yangdi capturing children to work on the Grand Canal; perhaps even earlier legends can be found.

The current legend of capturing souls in Shaoxing is slightly different from those in the past. In the past, it was consistently said to be capturing the souls of young children, but this time, it is the souls of women, children, the elderly, and the weak that are being captured, seemingly encompassing a much broader scope. Taoist philosophy, such as Lao-Zhuang, uses infants to symbolize the pure, uncarved innocence, the so-called "complete spirit." Later, honest people took the metaphors of intelligent people as actual facts. Thus, since the Han Dynasty, the cultivation of immortals has focused on infants: demons in caves treat young men and women as snacks; alchemists regard eating young boys' qi and virgin blood as medicinal ingredients. The Yellow Emperor ascended to heaven after copulating with eighty-one Su Nu, so old nuns in Suzhou and Master Duan of the Morality Society are searching everywhere for virgins, wanting to reach the perfect number of eighty-one. The methods may differ, but the principle is the same. The belief that major projects and constructions cannot succeed without using children to suppress evil is also a deduction from the same principle. However, the application of souls being extended to women, children, the elderly, and the weak seems a bit modernized and doesn't quite align with the theories of immortals. Moreover, with the people of Shaoxing promoting this, even middle-aged people like us feel a bit uneasy and apprehensive. I always feel that it's best not to expand the scope of employing souls!

Anecdotes from Medan 142

— Feier

As the train approached Medan Station, the "Temple of the Heavenly Queen," representing the beliefs of the Chinese, first came into the traveler's view with its ancient architectural style of red walls and pointed ridges. After getting off the train and walking past the Temple of the Heavenly Queen, the ancient bronze incense burner on the wide courtyard in front of the building was steadily emitting circles of smoke; a young woman wearing a sarong was inserting incense sticks into the incense burner. Upon entering the temple, on the right-hand wall, which was blackened by incense smoke, hung a bronze plaque engraved with the amounts donated by various wealthy people since the opening of Medan, starting with the Zhang family, as well as the names of the Chinese consular officials. Nearby, I also saw the "Guan Di Temple," which had a similar architectural style. The non-crude scale of these temples proclaimed that the power of the Chinese here was indeed great, and the deities here were enjoying "human" blessings, with the buildings being far grander than the "Bo Gong Palaces" and "San Bao Temples" scattered throughout the smaller ports. (Naturally, they could not compare to the "San Ling Temple" in Singapore or the "Kek Lok Si Temple" in Penang, which was all due to the control of human affairs.)

This spiritual burden represented the perseverance of the Chinese. (Or perhaps it was also the inferior side of the Chinese.) Relying on the blessings of the gods, the Chinese transformed wilderness into rich plains and turned harsh malaria-infested lands into paradises. Also relying on the blessings of the unseen gods, Medan was transformed from the hands of the Hakka Zhang family into the current city and became the capital of Sumatra Island. Unfortunately, the results of the labor were only harvested by others, and the Chinese only ate the leftovers of others. Medan has become a typical colonial city, and "San Bao Gong" and "Heavenly Queen, Guan Di" are no match for "Jesus, the Lord." Can gods urge people to build human culture, and can gods also protect their people from being bullied and confused by foreign races? In our corner of the world, will the overseas Chinese in Medan be able to free themselves from the intoxication of the gods amid the anti-Chinese voices and engage in human efforts?

In the center of Medan, the Chinese community leaders built the "Majoor's Residence." Stone lions stood in front of the gate, and the house diligently imitated the style of the residences of high-ranking officials and nobles in the imperial era. In this colony dominated by capitalist imperialism, the Chinese still retained the minds of the feudal era. A coolie, once he had obtained a relatively higher position through diligent labor and became a "Kapitan," felt joy in his heart and glory on his "face" that was just like that of the "scholar-official" class of the past. White people exploited this weakness, placing the "Majoors" and "Kapitans" under their control and assisting in colonial rule. There were many people from Fujian and Guangdong who served as guides for the Dutch, captured tribal settlements, and obtained the title of "Kapitan." After returning to their hometowns, they built solemn mansions and were called "So-and-So Sir," which was exactly the same situation.

Thinking about the grandson of Ye Lai in Kilongpo being forced to dedicate the territory and the King of Pontianak in Borneo (a Teochew person) being defeated by the Dutch due to lack of support, Java being filled with the "Red River," or groups of pioneers now being successively expelled back to their country, what will our thoughts be?

Within the Circle of Slowed Steps 143

— Written by Chen Jingsheng

Life 144

— Xijun

The youthful season has warm, fragrant dreams and also colorful aspirations, but after being trampled by the iron hooves of reality, it is immediately shattered.

I fear the ferocious face of life more than I fear ghosts and demons; it always follows me closely, never leaving me for even a moment. I seem to hear its cold laughter from time to time beside me, making my pores stand on end like the chirping of night ghosts. I know that it is chasing me so closely because it wants to seize me when I am negligent for once in a thousand times of being careful; then it will pounce on me and swallow me like a snack.

Under the scrutiny of such an insidious and ruthless life, I lowered my head silently, straightened my chest, like a camel, a cart, shouldering a heavy load of thousands of pounds, letting its whip beat me incessantly, driving me forward on a long, hazy, endless journey, regardless of day or night, from today to tomorrow, eternally trudging forward, sweating and panting. I cannot easily see the light of the sun, because even in the daytime, the space is still filled with thick fog; at night, there is no moon or stars in the sky, only the desolate wind is howling, and surrounding my body are layers of shadows. I crawl in the impenetrable shadows because I am already exhausted.

However, life will not show me any pity because of this; its whip continues to lash relentlessly. If my pace slows down even slightly, it will immediately lash me heavily, forcing me to hurry. So I walk silently, without a word, biting my teeth, enduring its insatiable trampling. Thus, my neck gradually bends down, and my chest also shrinks, unable to straighten up again.

"What can life give me?" I asked the terrifying life timidly, with a hysterical tone, almost losing my senses from being tortured. It only tightened its iron-blue face, laughing coldly, and did not pay attention to me. And at the same time, it raised its whip again.

Who says that the top of life is ironed with blue colors and splendid drawings? I do not believe it; these beautiful lines have never floated before my eyes, and I have never harbored this thought. I only know that life only gives me endless tribulations and hardships, making me its cattle and horse for a long time, torturing me every day until my last breath. I also thought about gathering my strength, rushing over and grabbing it to beat it up, resisting its unreasonable oppression, but unfortunately, my legs have become numb from labor, my arms are also cramping, and my strength is even more lacking. So I often grab my hair madly in the sleepless late nights, pound my chest hard, and shout miserably, "You have to let me rest for a while, I am almost unable to move." But life still ignores me, its mouth always hanging with a ferocious sneer, and by tomorrow, it will raise its whip and torment me again.

A Person's Death (Part 1) 145

— Hei Ying

One day, the tall, thin tailor with shoulders like pen rests in the shop fell ill. "You go and rest for a while!" the boss said, standing in front of him like issuing a decree, with his clumsy splayed feet. The patient then breathed a sigh of relief and packed up the scattered cloth scraps, scissors, needle cushions, and other items, dragging his slow, duck-like steps, swaying as he went upstairs. Watching his disappearing back into that room where sunlight never reached, I stood woodenly at the staircase entrance, remembering what he had casually said to me a few days ago.

"Kid! You stand as strong as an ox!" he said, revealing a hint of envy, his eyes fixed on my body. "You won't get sick. But I'm not the same... If you don't get sick, you naturally won't understand the suffering of that punishment; it's really unbearable... Moreover, humans are all callous and snobbish creatures; if you have money and you catch a little cold, someone will ask you if you feel well, if you need medicine. But if you're poor, who cares about you! People will let you hide in your room, not even looking at you, except when you're taken by the King of Hell, then they'll casually prepare a coffin for you... I've seen too much of this kind of world!"

He looked melancholic. Since he got sick a few months ago and the Javanese woman who lived with him abandoned him, his illness had not actually improved. But if he didn't work, he wouldn't have food to eat, so he had to struggle to get up and sit in front of the Singer sewing machine, pedaling the wheel with his weak feet. Now he had fallen again.

Yes, it's best for poor people to be stronger, otherwise no one will pay attention to you if you get sick. That night, after I closed the shop door and turned off all the lights, I tiptoed to his room. I thought he might be asleep; but the candle flame on the rectangular table in front of the bed was still flickering, and I could still hear intermittent groans from inside the yellow mosquito net reaching my eardrums.

"Lao Fang," I called softly.

"Oh, is that you?" He turned over, his listless eyes looking at my face. I sat sideways on the edge of the bed, covering him with the blanket.

"Are you sick... Do you want to buy some medicine? Oh, you haven't eaten yet, do you want..."

"My appetite is not good, no need... Can you check if there's any Ba Gua Dan in that drawer?" he pointed to the table.

I found him a package of Ba Gua Dan, handed it to him, and also brought a glass of boiled water. Outside, it was the quiet, desolate field of May, the wind blowing, the coconut tree leaves rustling. I stood on a stool and closed a window opposite the bed. Accompanying the patient there, I started to doze off. "You go to sleep, I also want to be quiet for a while!" he said to me, closing his eyelids. I put down the mosquito net for him, blew out the candle, and returned to my corner on the third floor.

One day, two days... The tailor's illness did not improve, and the groaning sounds gradually became heavier, making people unable to bear listening to them. I came to see him several times every day, bringing him porridge, buying medicine, opening the window, or sweeping the floor. Sometimes he complained to me, but later he lay weakly on the bed, his eyes staring straight at the top of the mosquito net, and he was too lazy to speak. The landlady always grabbed me to ask about the patient's condition, but she herself stayed far away from him. Her pockmarked face even showed a hateful expression, as if she couldn't wait to shout out loud: "What bad luck, there's a sick ghost living behind my room on the second floor, he's groaning every day, like the King of Hell is dragging him, it's so noisy that people can't sleep... What if he dies in our shop?" However, she didn't have the courage to shout out her concerns. She paced back and forth in the kitchen, muttering, "What to do?" While I was washing rice to prepare to cook, I secretly watched the woman's expression. Finally, she suddenly said to herself, "Why not go to the hospital?"

"Hospital? We don't have a hospital here!" I interjected.

"Send him to the hospital in Yalen," she said.

Night Crossing (12) 146

— Zhou Lengjia

Mr. Xunqing's expression at this time was hard to describe. His face reddened all the way to the roots of his ears, and the reddish patch on his right cheek was now even more translucent. Suddenly, he erupted in a rage and charged straight up to the young woman, saying:

"You fart! You are releasing the loudest, most unbearable skunk farts! Who do you think Jin Xunqing is? Me... Jin Xunqing... a former candidate for county councilor, now a well-known gentleman in the area, would I come to flirt with a worthless piece of trash like you? You dare to slander me publicly, it's outrageous! I bet you were molested by a robber, got your head turned by a ghost, and are now trying to stick to me!"

The young woman was forced back to her seat, continuing her weak and powerless sobs, not daring to speak again. Mr. Xunqing, having gained the upper hand, unleashed his authority even more, filling the entire cabin with his loud, hoarse voice.

"Hmph! You don't even recognize who Jin Xunqing is, and you dare to make trouble on my turf. I can't let you off! Do you know that you have committed a crime? There is a crime in criminal law called public defamation, which is what you have committed now. I won't say much to you, just according to Article... Article... of the criminal law, in short, it's a certain article of the criminal law, I'll sue you immediately! Hey, boatman!"

"What?" the boatman asked listlessly from the stern.

"Get me a long rope."

"Gah! We don't have that."

Liu Cangshui had already fully understood the situation. He felt somewhat indignant for the young woman and couldn't help but step forward and say to Mr. Xunqing:

"Mr. Xunqing, let it go. When it's time to be lenient, be lenient, and when you can forgive, forgive."

"No! Reputation is a person's second life. I don't care if she's a robber's bottom, but I can't tolerate her defaming my reputation!"

Wu Hexuan also seemed to be unable to stand Mr. Xunqing's domineering manner. He shouted at the boatman in a louder voice than Mr. Xunqing.

"Hey! Boatman, where are we?"

"Yangjia Ba is ahead."

"Good! Stop in Yangjia Ba for the night."

His words could almost represent the unanimous opinion of the entire boat, because no one in the cabin expressed any dissent.

A great silence enveloped the entire cabin, in which only the young woman's soft sobbing was faintly audible. (End)

Educational News

Ministry of Education Inspection: Shandong Province Vocational Education Report 147

An abstract of the Ministry of Education's inspection report on vocational education in Shandong Province is as follows: In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], there were a total of seven provincial vocational education institutions. As a result of mergers and closures in the 19th year [1930], there were three schools. By the 22nd year [1933], the Yanggu Dyeing and Weaving Vocational School was added, bringing the total to four schools. It was originally planned to add the Boshan Ceramics Vocational School in the 23rd year [1934], the Weixian Dyeing and Weaving Vocational School and the Yixian Mining Vocational School in the 24th year [1935], the Yantai Aquatic Products Vocational School and the Jinan Animal Husbandry and Horticulture Vocational School in the 25th year [1936], and the Linqing Agricultural Vocational School and the Jinan Civil Engineering Vocational School in the 26th year [1937], with a planned addition of seven schools in four years. It is stated that the Ceramics Vocational School was not established this year. It has been found that the allocation of secondary education funding in the province deviates greatly from the standards set by the Ministry. Even if the province's original plan is fully implemented, by the 16th year [presumably a typo for the intended 26th year] the vocational education funding would only account for 18%. Now that even this plan has not been implemented on schedule, it is truly regrettable. Recently, the province held a meeting of secondary school principals, and the Education Department proposed a plan to expand vocational education, intending to gradually close down the normal training institutes in various counties and establish joint vocational schools. Subsequently, in the name of the Secondary School Administrative Conference, a proposal was made to the provincial government to implement a "livelihood politics," formulating an industrial construction plan and types of vocational education facilities. This proposal has been included in the province's three-year plan currently under review. Whether it can be realized is unknown. The following are some points that deserve attention based on the inspection:

1. The province has abundant local products, and the promotion of vocational education should not be delayed. The recently drafted three-year industrial construction plan includes ten schools for the training of technical personnel. The types of departments offered are mostly the same as the province's original vocational education promotion plan. A direction should be determined immediately and implemented quickly, without further delay. Teacher training should also be prepared in advance.

2. The production quantity of each school is only equal to half of the material cost. For example, with 4,000 yuan of materials, only 2,000 yuan of finished products can be sold, and the rest is all consumption. This urgently needs to be improved.

3. The funding for vocational schools in the province has not yet been increased according to the prescribed standards, resulting in a severe shortage of school purchase funds. The remaining funds from the annual sales are often used. If vacation work is to be implemented and production is centralized, then large quantities of materials cannot be obtained. A way to increase funding should be found immediately.

4. The Jinan Junior Industrial Vocational School of Shandong Province has achieved some results, but the output is small and the technology is lacking, resulting in very few sales. Vacation internships should be implemented. Products such as candles made by the applied chemistry department have almost no sales due to the abundance of goods on the market. Attention should be paid to the manufacture of paint, ink, waxed paper, and leather, etc. Leather products are of poor quality and need to be improved urgently. The attached short-term dyeing and weaving class recruits elementary school graduates and older out-of-school people, graduates in one year, and focuses on technology, which is still effective and should continue to be run. It should also be renamed Vocational Training Class.

5. The Jinan Women's Junior Dyeing, Weaving, and Sericulture Vocational School of Shandong Province has good dyeing and weaving equipment and a large capacity. However, the woven products are mostly thin and not durable, and the output is also small. Concentrated practice should be implemented during the summer vacation of the second grade to achieve proficiency in skills. The sericulture department has simple equipment, no new-style machinery, and the results are mediocre. Recently, the Construction Department of the province is expanding the silkworm breeding experiment station, which requires a large number of people. The teaching content should be enriched and improvements should be sought. The attached third-grade mathematics students are determined to go to higher education and are unwilling to pay attention to practical training, which has a great impact on other students and should be strictly corrected. Those who hope to go to higher education, in addition to normal operations, are allowed to make up for it after class.

6. The dyeing and weaving achievements of the Jining Junior Industrial Vocational School of Shandong Province are good, but the output is not large enough and more practice should be added. The chemical engineering equipment is simple and urgently needs to be added. The finished products such as leather paint are also too rough. Most students are willing to work hard. The recruitment and training methods of the training class are the same as the above two schools and should be renamed Vocational Training Class and continue to be run.

7. Licheng County Junior Industrial Vocational School is entirely funded and established by the county, divided into applied chemistry and mechanical engineering departments. The equipment has a foundation and the operation is in accordance with the regulations. There are currently four classes, which are barely sufficient. When the number of classes increases in the future, they must continue to be enriched. The annual recurring expenses can be increased to more than 19,000 yuan when six classes are handled, but the material cost is less than 30 yuan per class per month, which is very difficult, resulting in most of the expenses required for all exercises being paid by teachers who purchase the manufactured products, raising capital and purchasing raw materials, which is not a long-term solution. The department should provide appropriate subsidies year by year to maintain and seek progress. The school's enrollment quota stipulates that Licheng must account for half of the number, and the remaining foreign students are not allowed to replace Licheng students if Licheng County cannot recruit enough. Currently, there are only more than 80 students in total, which is probably due to this and is very uneconomical. The county should be ordered to change its methods, stipulating that students with Licheng County citizenship have priority, but if the quota in this county is insufficient, foreign students are allowed to supplement it in order to enrich the number of students. Also, some students in the school are too young, not strong enough, and feel a little difficult to work. Ways should be found to adjust this.

8. The private Huilu Vocational School of Industry and Commerce has clean and useful school buildings, and the teaching is relatively earnest. However, the educational facilities in the elementary classes are aimed at entering the senior classes of this school, and general subjects account for almost two-thirds of the entire teaching, which is not appropriate. Commercial training should be increased to make elementary education a stage so that students with economic difficulties have the opportunity to earn a living. Those who wish to enter senior classes can also shorten the course by one year depending on the circumstances, which is different from recruiting junior high school students. The school has not yet been registered and should be done as soon as possible. The name of the school should also be changed. Commercial vocational schools should not be confused with industrial and commercial vocational schools.

9. The private Huishang Vocational School is extremely lacking in equipment and the operation is illegal. The teaching methods and spirit of each department are improper. The attached commercial normal department, in fact, completely prepares ordinary elementary school teachers, which is even more inappropriate and should be improved within a limited time, otherwise, it will be ordered to stop.

10. The Provincial Public Experimental School has four groups: dyeing and weaving, printing, applied chemistry, and embroidery. Except for dyeing and weaving, the others are too simple. Classes are held in shifts in the morning and afternoon, with two-thirds of the time for public education and one-third for vocational training. It is said that most students can use what they have learned to earn a living. It seems that the equipment should be enriched and reorganized into a vocational training school to match the name.

11. The Department of Education and Industry has established a laboratory instrument and biology specimen manufacturing institute, specializing in the preparation of instruments and specimens for all elementary schools and part of junior high schools, which are sold at low prices to improve primary and secondary education. The intention is very good. It has been found that the number of primary schools in the province has increased sharply in recent years, and the content needs to be improved. The establishment of this manufacturing institute by the department to enrich scientific equipment is an urgent matter. However, the tools are not yet complete and the products are not refined enough. The person in charge should be ordered to go to the scientific instrument and specimen manufacturing institutes in various places to study in detail and strive for improvement. When the operation is successful in the future, the content can be expanded and attention can be paid to the manufacture of standard tools for labor science in primary and secondary schools to improve labor education.

12. The Agricultural College of Shandong University has been engaged in the study of fertilizer application, plowing and planting of cotton seeds, and pests and diseases of taro seedlings in recent years, and has achieved considerable results. In order to promote the research results, training courses have been held in Laiyang, Licheng, and other regions, recruiting young farmers to provide them with useful agricultural remedial education, which has also been effective. However, due to economic difficulties, it is impossible to expand the facilities and appropriate subsidies can be given as needed to promote it. Recently, the university has cooperated with three provincial rural teachers' schools to enrich the content of agricultural subjects. The method is very good and should be stepped up.
