Kiangsu Boy Scout Grand Review and Camping 151

Registration and Camping Advanced to the End of September; Review Schedule and Methods Have Been Drafted

(Chenkiang News) Because the National Boy Scout Second Grand Review and Camping is scheduled to be held on October 6th, the Kiangsu Provincial Boy Scout Council will officially start working on the Advance Review and Camping Committee from the 10th. The schedule and methods are as follows:

(Grand Review Schedule) Registration and camping on the morning of September 30th, replenishment of camp construction in the afternoon, and group leader talks in the evening. Opening ceremony drill in the morning of October 1st, review exercise drill in the afternoon, speech contest campfire party in the evening. Skills contest in the morning of October 3rd, skills contest sightseeing in the afternoon, lantern parade in the evening. Camp dismantling in the morning of October 4th, closing ceremony in the afternoon.

(Campfire Party Methods) (1) Date and Location: 7:30 PM on October 1st and 2nd, held at the Provincial Stadium. (2) Grouping: Held separately by elementary and middle schools. (3) Participating Programs: Each group participates in recreational activities, with a maximum of two programs per group, and each program should not exceed ten minutes. (4) Performance Order: Arranged by this committee and should not be changed. (5) Performance Supplies: Prepared by each group. (6) Registration: The programs and number of participants in each group must be reported to the assembly group on time, otherwise, they will not be allowed to participate. (7) Performance Evaluation: The quality of the performances of each group will be evaluated by the Grand Review and Camping Evaluation Committee.

(Lantern Parade Methods) (1) Date: 7:00 PM on October 3rd. (2) Route: Depart from the Provincial Stadium, pass through Chungcheng Road, Yentou Street, and out of Lao West Gate, pass through West Gate Main Street, Bosen Road, Pao-kai Road, Chungshan Road, and South Gate Street, out of South Gate and back to the camp. (3) Participants: All Boy Scouts participating in the Provincial Grand Review and Camping, except for guards, must participate, led by the group leader. (4) Command: One chief commander, concurrently held by the chief commander of the review, and one deputy commander, concurrently held by the director of the assembly group. (5) Arrangement: Arranged according to group order and should not be disordered. (6) Registration: The number of participants in each group must be reported to the assembly group on time, otherwise, they will not be allowed to participate. (7) Lanterns and solder are prepared by each group, but they must be rich in the meaning of promoting the New Life Movement. (8) Performance Evaluation: The quality of the lanterns of each group will be evaluated by the Grand Review and Camping Evaluation Committee.

Annual Merit-Based Pay Increase for Teachers in Hangchow Elementary Schools, Chekiang Province 152

From the 17th year [1928] to the 22nd year [1933], the number of teachers in Hangchow Municipal Elementary Schools who received annual merit-based pay increases reached a maximum of 308, and the amount of the pay increases was nearly 10,000 yuan. The reason for this was the increase in the number of classes. The annual merit-based pay increases spent in the first and second halves of the 23rd year [1934] were all over 10,000 yuan. Almost all of the more than 80 municipal elementary schools have teachers who received this preferential treatment.

Page 12

Economic Special Issue

Discussion on the Opinion of Issuing Commodity Securities 166

— Wang Yutong

The stability of a country's economy depends on a sound monetary policy. In recent years, China's economic situation has been chaotic, almost entirely affected by unsound monetary policies. Silver, in China, is the sole standard currency, while in other countries, it is regarded merely as a commodity. Therefore, during the past years of the gold expensive and silver cheap trend, our economic circles were severely influenced by other factors, further inflicting deep pain on the silver standard. The United States's aim in raising the price of silver was to universally increase the world's silver price, so that gold prices would fall and commodity prices would gradually and progressively increase. Its sole purpose was to increase the purchasing power of silver standard countries to improve its own foreign trade. However, the result may not have matched its expectations. The price of silver has indeed seen a universal increase worldwide, but the increase in the purchasing power of silver standard countries, from the perspective of gold standard countries, can be theoretically affirmed, but in practice, it has been the opposite. For example, today, China is experiencing a rise in the value of currency due to the increase in the price of silver, directly leading to a drop in commodity prices, economic recession, and declining purchasing power. All of these are practical evidences. Especially recently, China's silver reserves have been lured by the US silver purchase policy, resulting in a large outflow. It is a natural result that monetary tightening has become more profound. The implementation of this type of silver purchase policy is only harmful to China's monetary system, harming others without benefiting oneself. I do not know why the US government adopted the policy of raising the price of silver. Therefore, commentators generally believe that China's adoption of the silver standard currency is no longer in line with the times. However, the gold exchange standard promoted by Mr. Kemmerer is also difficult to realize. Various paper currency standards also have no hope of being implemented in China. As a result, China's monetary system still cannot but base its foundation on metals. Among advanced countries, some can maintain the gold standard with only a 30% gold reserve. If China has sound banks, unifies paper currency, and maintains credit in the future, then the silver standard system can still continue. However, based on the current situation, the implementation of the silver purchase policy remains unchanged, and it has not been slightly altered, but has become even more intensified. On the one hand, China wants to reorganize its currency system to maintain the silver standard, but this cannot be achieved overnight. Therefore, in recent years, there has been a prevailing argument among people in China's economic circles advocating for a currency revolution. Mr. Xu Qingfu, in his books "An Economic Revolution to Save the Country," strongly advocated for thorough progress, with thorough ideals and meticulous organization, showing unique insights. Later, Mr. Yan Baichuan gave a speech on issuing commodity securities and has piloted rural credit cooperative bonds in Xinxian and Wutai in Shanxi Province. Recently, I was fortunate to receive an article written by Mr. Xu Qingfu, "Opinions on Issuing Commodity Securities." Mr. Xu deeply feels that China's production is backward, international trade is in a deficit position, and silver, as the raw material of China's currency, is always sought from abroad, increasing the amount of imports. Therefore, he advocates issuing commodity securities, which can also make the currency abundant and link currency with commodity prices, so that commodity prices do not increase due to the increase in the amount of currency. This will increase production, increase the effect of actual distribution, increase the amount of consumption, and achieve the purpose of economic improvement. Mr. Qingfu is an economist in China, and an outstanding figure in our party. I recently received his great work, and after repeated discussions, I deeply admire him. However, there are still a few points that I would like to discuss with Mr. Qingfu.

The issuance of commodity securities must be preceded by a large-scale national survey and statistics of commodities. For the country's commodities, their production situation, supply and demand relationship, and value must be precisely measured and statistically analyzed. In addition, the transportation and transaction procedures for various commodities are different, and there are also seasonal and regional differences, with quality changes depending on the climate and season. All of these should be considered thoroughly. Secondly, the implementation of the commodity securities system will bring about significant changes to the economic lives of the middle and upper classes. They are accustomed to consuming refined commodities, mainly imported goods. Now, the commodities represented by commodity securities are all domestically produced goods. The implementation of the commodity securities system for the general public is to prevent the superior economic life of the middle and upper classes, reduce their material enjoyment, and force them to conform to the general economic life. Under today's complex economic situation in China, it is uncertain whether this can be promoted smoothly. Mr. Xu also said, "For the foreign goods we need, apart from those with limited underground reserves and special products due to the relationship between weather and geography, most can be imitated... If the commodity securities system is implemented, they can safely produce them, and products that do not exist now can also be produced, so there is no need to rely on foreigners." This is indeed what we want to achieve. However, in reality, China's material progress today is not as good as others, and its science and technology are also backward. Ordinary foreign goods can barely be imitated, but those that are refined and have specialized characteristics have all sorts of problems in terms of technology and raw materials. If we still use the old methods of purchasing raw materials from abroad, or partially manufactured products, and hiring foreign technicians to specialize in imitation, then the payment for raw materials and the salaries of foreign technicians will have a close relationship with the currency system. Moreover, under the current precarious state of China's entire national economy, it cannot tolerate the existence of such imitation industries. Furthermore, the importance of the gradual development of material enjoyment should also be considered. In other words, the era is continuously advancing, and human material desires are also progressing day by day. If it is small, it is enough to help the intelligence and skills of human beings to become more refined; if it is large, it can make the cause flourish. Since the number of people can survive with the transformation of the era, they must also conform to the material enjoyment of the era to match it. Material civilization is indeed sufficient to constitute the elements of national survival. Therefore, at the beginning of the implementation of the commodity securities system, it is not advisable to excessively suppress the general material desires, otherwise, it will be like cutting the feet to fit the shoes, and the benefits will not be commensurate with the harm that follows. My intention in making these remarks is not to speak up for the middle and upper classes who enjoy a superior life, but I also feel that the implementation of economic policies should strive to avoid actions that are contrary to economic principles.

Mr. Xu said, "When implementing the commodity securities system, we must control all production sectors." This is indeed the key point. The scope of industrial control is extremely large. I will only briefly mention a few points that must be known about commodity production and sales control:

1. Control of Commodity Production: (A) Quality Control, (B) Seed Quality Control, (C) Specification Control,

2. Control of Prices and Sales: (A) Price Control, (B) Sales Price Ratio Control,

3. Control of Production Volume and Supply and Demand: (A) Production Volume Control, (B) Transportation Volume Control,

4. Control of Raw Material Procurement,

Therefore, in industrial control legislation, if it is crude and unrefined, the effect of control will not be seen, and it will have a great impact on the entire commodity securities system. This must be paid attention to. The above is only a brief expression of my humble opinion. In the future, if there is a chance, I would like to have a detailed discussion with Mr. Qingfu to seek his advice. -- May 22, 1935, in Beiping

Improvements in Rural Ding County, Hebei 167

— Lu Shaoliu

Ding County is a special experimental county designated by the Hebei Provincial County Administration Construction Research Institute. All undertakings within the county—particularly in the realm of rural economics—are being vigorously implemented after careful research by various experts. Many projects are now demonstrably underway and progressing forward, thereby stirring the interest of observers from both China and abroad. In recent years, the number of visitors has been no fewer than several hundred. The following is a brief description of the recent general situation in rural Ding County for the reference of those concerned about and studying rural issues:

The total land area is 3,650 square miles. According to a 1934 survey by the Rural Reconstruction Movement (Pingmin Jiaoyu Chujinhui), 1.6 million mu of farmland have already been cultivated. Distributing this land among the county's large population of 400,000 people results in an average of only four mu per person. This is a startling difference when compared to the fact that English farmers need 15 mu of land per person to maintain a living, and American farmers need 16.09 mu per person to break even. Therefore, the underlying difficulty in the past lives of Ding County farmers was the triad of “large population, limited land, and insufficient grain distribution.” However, they have managed to survive peacefully until now, though it is easy to imagine how low their standard of living must be. Recently, well-digging has become exceptionally developed in the county (according to the results of an inspection by Zhang Houwan from the Civil Affairs Department this year, the whole county has more than 60,000 surplus laborers; see the May 27th issue of *Ta Kung Pao*), which has greatly increased farmers' productivity. As a result, a substantial amount of agricultural produce is exported annually via the Pinghan Railway.

The county lacks high mountains and large rivers. The plains are vast and seemingly endless. The fertile soil is quite suitable for cultivation. Due to the similar environmental conditions in each village, all farmland relies on well irrigation. (According to the 1934 survey by the Rural Reconstruction Movement, there were 50,000 wells; according to a recent inspection by Zhang Cunwan, Director of the Hebei Civil Affairs Department, the whole county has 60,000 wells; see the May 27th issue of *Ta Kung Pao*.) Even in years without rain, farmers can still plant and sow as usual. Therefore, there is a saying: "Ding County never dies from drought, while Qu Yang never fills from floods." There are two types of wells: pulley wells and waterwheel wells. Because waterwheel wells are more difficult to dig, they are less common, accounting for about a quarter of the total. Waterwheels mostly use livestock power to draw water. Pulley wells rely entirely on human power to turn the crank. Waterwheel wells have twice the water output of pulley wells. On average, each pulley well can irrigate two mu, while a waterwheel can irrigate seven or eight mu. In dry weather, each well can irrigate about one mu in rotation. Recently, the North China Water Conservancy Commission and the China, Hebei, and Jinpo Banks have separately offered well-digging loans at 8% interest, repayable in three years. It is reported that many farmers have already taken out loans to dig wells. In the future, the increase in the number of wells will certainly lead to a large increase in agricultural production. As such, the problem of "large population, limited land" for Ding County farmers should be resolved, barring unforeseen natural disasters or man-made calamities. The automatic water pump invented by the Livelihood Education Department of the Rural Reconstruction Movement has also been successfully tested. It is estimated that each machine can irrigate four mu of land per day. It consists of an endless chain with long handles placed on top. Once the chain is cranked, it rotates continuously, and water is sprayed upwards from the chain's empty spaces. The machine parts are so easy to operate that children of fourteen or fifteen years old can crank it. It is more labor-saving than ordinary waterwheels or pulley wells, and the amount of water drawn is also greater than that of waterwheels. Currently, four machines have been transported separately to Buluogang and Jianyang county villages to help farmers irrigate their fields. If they can be promoted on a large scale in the future, it will certainly be good news for the farmers of Ding County!

The county is divided into five districts, with a total of 472 villages of various sizes. The farmers' lifestyles are generally the same. Except for the Gaojiazhuang area in the fourth district, which resembles Qu Yi, the rest all follow a very simple way of life, wearing cloth clothes and eating vegetables, living in harmonious joy. Under the old rule of "working at sunrise and resting at sunset," they do not consider it a hardship to sweat and toil. The amount of the year's harvest determines their regular expenses throughout the year. If it is still insufficient, they must find a way to engage in side occupations or seek other work as compensation. Their daily food is mainly millet, supplemented by vegetables. Non-wealthy families rarely eat wheat flour. They usually eat three meals a day, but only two meals during the winter slack season. Most of the surplus grain is stored for consumption during the busy farming season in the coming year. Furthermore, eight or nine out of ten people only boil a few pieces of sweet potatoes and yams for their two meals, drinking plain water with their food. Their standard of living is truly pitiful. However, their habit of frugality is a unique virtue of the farmers of Ding County. Their clothing is even simpler, mostly purple-flowered homespun cloth woven by their own women. Each set of clothes is not easily replaced until it is worn to tatters and can no longer be mended. Although women in the city have recently been influenced by new trends and mostly pursue fashionable clothing and purchase foreign goods, according to a recent survey, the total value of women's ornaments imported annually exceeds 180,000 yuan. It is difficult to find even one woman with bound feet (under the age of twenty) walking through the streets and alleys. Most of the residential houses have flat roofs, built entirely of bricks, stones, and adobe. The walls are exceptionally sturdy. Each room must have an earthen pit. Ordinary five-member families mostly have four or five rooms, which are not crowded. However, there are very few windows, making it difficult for air to circulate, and the light is mostly dark, which is not in line with hygiene. Farmers are most compelled by life in spring, autumn, and during the wheat harvest, and they are extremely willing to work hard no matter how busy they are. Occasionally, in addition to harvesting their own crops, they also take the time to pick up the ears of grain left behind in other people's fields. Usually, eight or nine out of ten women go to the fields to help with the work, which is admirable compared to other counties where women are ashamed to go to the fields. Therefore, most women in the fields can crank the pulley to irrigate the fields and use hoes and shovels to till the land. The people's nature is straightforward and honest, which is well-known throughout North China, hence their tendency to litigate. They often engage in years of litigation over extremely trivial matters, causing them to become impoverished and bankrupt. It is said that there is hardly a village in the county without lawsuits (litigation), and some villages have more than one or two cases. The former county magistrate, Huo Liuding, once issued a notice advising farmers to stop suing. The text included the line, "A certain person from Ding County is quick-tempered and starts sixteen lawsuits a day..." which serves as clear evidence. It is said that the total annual cost of litigation exceeds 800,000 yuan (including appeals). This staggering cost of lawsuits is truly a major cause of rural economic bankruptcy.

Affected by economic bankruptcy, the value of land in the county has plummeted in recent years. Land that was worth 100 yuan per mu four or five years ago is now reduced to 20 or 30 yuan, and no one even asks about it, making it impossible for farmers to sell. As a result, responsible families declare bankruptcy, with as many as eight families doing so in a single year in the small village of Baihu, west of the city. To cope with this difficulty, the former county magistrate, Huo Liuding, ordered farmers in various villages to organize debt mediation committees to clean up their debts on their own, but this was not very effective. Fortunately, this spring, China, Jincheng, and Hebei Banks implemented loans totaling 800,000 yuan. The countryside has slightly revived economically due to this large amount of funds. Recently, the county government has also been urgently seeking to promote the organization of cooperative societies, which farmers join voluntarily. All matters related to farmers' livelihoods are centered on the cooperative societies, including cooperative loans, cooperative purchasing, and cooperative marketing. If this yields results in the future, the benefits to farmers will certainly be substantial. The rural produce, wheat, millet, rice, and beans, are all produced in large quantities, followed by corn and sorghum. According to the Rural Reconstruction Movement's 1934 general survey, the total annual production of millet was 6.11 million dan, and the total annual production of wheat was 4.34 million dan. In addition to being consumed by farmers in large quantities, the export value reached 300,000 yuan. Recently, the production of cotton and peanuts has increased sharply. Last year, the production of cotton reached 7.8 million dan, more than double the previous year. The production of peanuts reached 80 million kilograms, an increase of two-thirds over the previous year. Most of it is purchased by large merchants from Beijing and Tianjin and transported to various domestic and foreign locations for sale. In addition, Chinese cabbage and Ya pears are also special products, with a total annual production value of no less than 1 million yuan. Recently, the "drought-resistant millet" trial planted by the Livelihood Department of the Rural Reconstruction Movement has been successfully tested. This millet has a natural drought resistance ability and saves half the water compared to other millets. It has now been continuously trial planted by village cooperative societies. If it can be promoted in the future, farmers' food supply can be greatly increased, which would also be a great blessing for the people's food supply. The most common rural side occupations currently are handicrafts, pig farming, and salt leaching. Handicrafts are most developed in weaving cloth and making vermicelli, which do not stop even during the busiest farming season. It is estimated that the total annual output of cloth is 3 million yuan (according to the Rural Reconstruction Movement's survey). The materials are all cotton grown by the farmers themselves. The production methods are all manual. Each bolt of cloth can make a profit of one jiao in addition to the cost of labor and materials. In addition to being worn by farmers, most of it is sold by cloth merchants from the Zhangjiakou area and transported by camel to the northwest for sale, with a total annual export value of 200,000 yuan. The total annual production of vermicelli reaches 5 million kilograms. In addition to being consumed in this county, most of it is transported by carts to Shenze and Anguo counties and resold in the Daqing River, Ziya River, and Grape River basins. However, most of it is sweet potato vermicelli. The production method involves mashing sweet potatoes, crushing them with a stone mill, and placing them in a wooden sieve to extract the powder, which is made into a paste and dripped into a pot of boiling water and taken out to form vermicelli. This is most common in the villages in the southwest area, accounting for almost four-fifths of the villages, and is the farmers' only side occupation. Unfortunately, most of it is done manually, adhering to old methods without knowing how to improve them. Production is a major part of the county government's six major constructions. Those in charge should urgently find ways to improve it and use machinery to increase production. This is not only related to farmers' livelihoods but also greatly benefits the hygiene of vermicelli food, which is essential for our daily lives. Because farmers operate vermicelli workshops, almost eight or nine out of ten raise pigs. Usually, walking casually into any village, you can easily see groups of three or five pigs (except in Muslim villages). This is because raising pigs can not only get a high price but also provide much-needed fertilizer for farmland by feeding them the residue left over from vermicelli production, watering them with vermicelli soup. The pigs grow very quickly. When the pigs are fattened, each pig can usually be sold for ten yuan. In addition to being consumed in the county, most of it is purchased by local merchants and transported to Beijing and Tianjin for sale, commonly called "walking Beijing pigs." Each pig can earn five jiao, with an annual export value of approximately 150,000 yuan. Recently, the Rural Reconstruction Movement Farm's "Boar Hybrid Pigs" have been successfully tested and are vigorously promoted. Farmers in various villages are vying to buy them, but because they are very large and develop quickly, they must have a large amount of feed to be raised well.

The excess population and difficulty in making a living in this county is a very serious reality. As a result, most ambitious men (they do not necessarily have farmland) go out to seek their fortunes one after another. Most of them go to the three northeastern provinces, hence the slogan "going down to Guandong." Some engage in business, while others reclaim land and work. They all gather and return after autumn. In total, there are always fifty to sixty thousand people each year. Their hard-earned wages are usually around eighty yuan. After the September 18th Incident, the national crisis was serious, and farmers could not go out, which invisibly increased the number of unemployed farmers who needed to be fed in Ding County, which was also a major cause of rural collapse. According to a survey by the Rural Reconstruction Movement, the number of people privately appointed by traitors in the spring of 1934 was no less than 20,000, but most of them were deceived by foremen, and many families are still suing.

Because the farmers in this county are forced by life to have no money to buy edible salt, and because a small number of lands have a salty taste due to geological reasons, many villagers sweep the soil and leach salt, making it their only way to make a living. For example, along the north bank of the Shahe River in the first district, the northeast of the second district, the south of the third district, the northwest of the fourth district, and the west of the fifth district, approximately sixty villages all have privately set up salt pans to leach salt. On average, one hundred catties of soil can be leached into two dan of salt water, which can be dried into twenty catties of salt and eight catties of saltpeter. According to the price, salt is worth one yuan, while saltpeter is more than ten times higher, worth three or four yuan. Therefore, leaching one hundred catties of soil can earn a total of five yuan, which is far more profitable than planting crops by ten times. Therefore, the farmers in these villages are willing to sacrifice planting to maintain their livelihoods, and they must leach salt privately, even after being repeatedly punished by the stationed Ding County Anti-Smuggling Brigade.

In addition, the prevalence of drugs and the heavy exploitation of exorbitant taxes are also major causes of the rural depression. According to those familiar with the situation in the county, almost every village has people who smoke and sell opium, especially in the city. It is estimated that the annual consumption is around one million yuan (the number surveyed by Huo Liuding when he took over the county the year before last). Such a shocking amount is truly a major cause of rural bankruptcy. The land tax in Ding County, in addition to the regular amount, has additional surcharges and taxes that exceed double the amount. On average, each person bears more than one yuan. At this time of people's lack of livelihood and rural bankruptcy, abolishing exorbitant taxes is a proper priority. The Hebei Donation Tax Management Council has recently sent a letter requesting that the first phase of Ding County's exorbitant taxes, totaling 9,610 yuan, be abolished. Although the amount is not much, if it can be implemented, it can slightly alleviate the people's difficulties.

The above is a disorganized and casual writing about the current situation, past conditions, and causes of collapse in rural Ding County, which is truly laughable. However, Ding County is an experimental county, and its general situation can represent the North China region, so everything is worth our study. Therefore, I have drafted this article, despite its simplicity, in order to elicit further insights.

The Trend of Currency Issues (Continued and Concluded) 168

— Gan Cisen

—Also Discussing the Future of the Franc—

2. Exchange Restriction—Methods of restricting or suppressing the freedom of foreign exchange transactions are divided into five types: A. Restriction of capital movement—In a free capital market, the movement of international capital is unhindered; however, under a managed currency system, there are various methods to restrain the movement of capital: (1) Restricting the purchase of foreign exchange, (2) Restricting the purchase of foreign securities, (3) Restricting the export of raw gold and silver, and domestic and foreign banknotes. B. Restricting speculation, in three aspects: (1) Restricting domestic residents from purchasing foreign exchange, (2) Restricting domestic residents from trading spot and forward foreign exchange for foreigners, (3) Restricting domestic residents from lending national currency credit to foreigners. C. Restricting domestic residents from holding foreign currency, in two ways: (1) Forcing domestic residents to hand over foreign currency obtained from exports, (2) Forcing domestic residents to hand over bank deposits and securities held abroad. D. Restricting the repayment of foreign debts, also in three ways: (1) Suspending the transfer of foreign credit, (2) Retaining foreign credit within the country, (3) Restricting importers from purchasing foreign currency.

3. Gold Policy—The normal gold policy of various countries is to purchase gold in order to stabilize the currency value by enriching their reserves. Examples include Japan's Gold Holding Act, gold purchase policy, and the United States' purchase and subsidization of raw gold and silver production. In extraordinary times, the following methods are used: A. Taxing to equalize cash transportation points, B. Changing the official purchase price, C. Lowering the gold parity.

4. Exchange Clearing System—This system allows international credits and debts to be settled without foreign exchange procedures. The method is that the central banks of the countries concerned usually keep accounts in their respective national currencies, mutually clearing all international lending and borrowing arising from international trade. In other words, export proceeds must be offset against import proceeds from another country, eliminating the need for foreign exchange receipts and payments. This method can be implemented bilaterally between two countries or multilaterally between three countries.

5. Exchange Equalization Funds—A fund is established by a country's financial authorities specifically for the purpose of equalizing foreign exchange, as practiced in the United Kingdom and the United States. This method involves the central bank purchasing foreign exchange during export booms and selling foreign exchange during import booms, as a means of adjustment.

(4) The Scars of Sacrifice

At a time when countries are unanimously abandoning the gold standard, implementing a managed currency system, and using currency warfare to invade markets and stimulate production, only the gold bloc centered on France still maintains its "glorious isolation," guarding the bulwark of the gold standard.

However, this conservatism is exchanged for a huge sacrifice. By the time it obtains "glory," it is already scarred, and the general public has suffered greatly.

If we examine the scars of these "glorious isolationists," we can refer to the following figures.

Wholesale Price Index of Gold Bloc Countries (1913=100)

1919 1920 1921 1922 1923 1924

France 217.3 222.5 101.9 86.8 80.9 76.4

Belgium 212.9 108.4 90.2 77.2 72.3 68.0

Italy 481.0 411.0 342.0 110.0 282.0 276.0

Netherlands 142.0 227.0 97.0 79.0 74.0 78.0

Industrial Production Index of Gold Bloc Countries (1928=100)

1929 1930 1931 1932 1933 1934

France 109.4 110.2 97.6 77.6 84.3 78.4

Belgium 101.1 89.8 82.8 69.9 71.7 61.3

Italy 109.2 100.3 84.7 73.0 80.5 87.1

Netherlands 102.5 93.7 81.0 63.9 70.9 70.9

Note: According to the League of Nations Monthly Bulletin of Statistics

Just by looking at the wholesale price index and industrial production index of the gold bloc countries, we can understand the downward trend after the panic began. The situation in the past two years is in stark contrast to countries that have abandoned the gold standard. For example, the wholesale price index in the United States increased from 94.5 the year before last to 107.2 last year, and the United Kingdom also increased from 100.9 to 104.0. In terms of international trade, bankruptcies, and unemployment, countries that abandoned the gold standard all showed improvement or improvement, while countries that did not abandon the gold standard were "getting worse and worse." No wonder Professor Cassel (A.Caosel) said that the inability to restore the world economy is due to the gold bloc countries' reluctance to maintain the gold standard.

(5) The Future Trend—What is the future of the Franc?

Since Belgium abandoned the gold standard in March of this year, the Netherlands is also precarious: people's attention is focused on the franc, thinking that since the gold bloc has been differentiated, the future of the French gold standard is also in imminent danger.

Judging from the general economic situation in France, from the difficulties in French finances, or from the large outflow of gold from French reserves, anyone has reason to prove that the future of the franc is not so secure. According to the *Shen Pao* on May 27, the Banque de France lost as much as 30 million pounds of gold to the United States alone since May 8. At the same time, "the deficit in the French budget is 135 million pounds, and the financial panic it has encountered is unprecedented since Poincaré took office." - *Shen Pao*, May 18.

However, will this only surviving authoritative currency really collapse from this? I am afraid no one dares to answer. We know that the stability of the franc has its own special foundation. If we want to explore its safety, in addition to the surface phenomena, we must also understand this special foundation.

First, observe from the perspective of French traditional policy. Since the war, the French people have suffered greatly from the expansion of the franc. Since the franc savior Poincaré reorganized it in 1928, it has gradually stabilized; and they are especially afraid of the old pain. Therefore, the French government and people unanimously safeguard the safety of the franc and oppose its abandonment of the gold standard or devaluation. Successive cabinets have clearly expressed their determination to maintain the franc. Whenever a financial bill is passed by the parliament, the parliament and the government work together to reduce the budget in order to maintain the balance of payments and avoid the expansion of the franc. According to reports, French finances are experiencing great difficulties this time, but the government's expression to the outside world is still determined to maintain the safety of the franc (*Shen Pao*, May 28).

Secondly, observe from the perspective of the French economic structure. France is different from other countries. For example, the goal of the United Kingdom and the United States in abandoning the gold standard is to increase prices, stimulate production, and increase exports on the one hand; and to reduce the debt burden of domestic debtors by devaluing the currency on the other. Private debt in the United States reaches 70,000,000,000 US dollars, and this debt is mostly dispersed among countless small debtors, while the creditors are concentrated in a few financial institutions. France has very little private debt, and the people mostly invest in government bonds, so its debt is the government's debt to the people. Therefore, the devaluation of the currency by the United States to reduce debt is welcomed by the general public; in France, it is opposed by the general public.

Finally, in terms of the abundance of French gold reserves, France does not need to abandon the gold standard. Until the end of last year, France's gold reserves never fell below 800 million francs, and the ratio to the amount of banknotes in circulation also never fell below 70%. (According to the International League of Nations Statistical Monthly Report) We know that there are two ways for cash to flow out: one is to exchange banknotes for cash or take cash with checks, and the other is for France to export cash itself to repay international debts. Judging from the current situation, the latter is impossible, and the former means that the cash decreases, that is, the debt also decreases accordingly, without any loss to the storage reserves. According to recent telegrams, "officials are convinced that the government will not suppress the value of the franc, because the gold reserves still have 110 million pounds, which is enough to meet any emergency" (*Shen Pao*, May 28), which is proof of this.

Having said that, my point is not that the position of the franc is still absolutely safe now. Because we know that all traditional policies are not immutable, and even the most solid forces do not have the power to change the world to compensate for the huge gap in finance. And the so-called protection of the interests of the majority of farmers and wealthy securities holders will ultimately not be able to resist the decline of the entire industrial economy and the suffering of large numbers of unemployed workers. In addition to this, there are also accusations from other countries; then, even if France can still wear the tattered clothing of the gold standard, what is the point?

The Banque de France has always been called a bottomless gold vault, and the strong holding of gold is naturally a point it can be proud of. However, according to foreign telegrams, the cash lost from March 29 of last year to the present has reached 2,372,000,000 francs (*Shen Pao*, May 27). In recent days, speculators have been even more active, and by the end of this month, it may be more than that. The Banque de France's discount rate has increased from two and a half to four percent, and it is said that there is still a possibility of increasing, and the helplessness is also visible in general.

My conclusion is that the gold standard of the franc may be maintained temporarily, but if the general economic situation does not improve, then abandonment is only a matter of time. The future of world currency may only be seen in banknotes before long; at that time, the world's economists should be asked to talk about the world's standard system again. -May 28, 1935-

Commercial News

Finance The Foreign Exchange Market Remains Dull and Stagnant 169

Call Loan Rates and Auxiliary Coinage Remain Calm

Recently, the foreign exchange market of banks has been affected by tension. Trading among financial institutions has been reluctant to proceed, resulting in a dull and stagnant situation. Yesterday was also Sunday, making the market even more desolate. The call loan rate in the foreign exchange market remained at 1.8% in both the morning and afternoon, unchanged from the previous day. Call loan transactions amounted to over 2.5 million in the morning trading, with new transactions exceeding 300,000. Afternoon trading was quiet. Transactions in the Small General Association totaled over 500,000. Money shops remitted over 18 million in foreign public notes, with remittances from various routes exceeding 200,000. Inflow from other sources was over 100,000. Transactions in foreign exchange suppression were over 100,000. There were no banknote transactions for withdrawals; in terms of issuance, only privately marked notes amounted to over 400,000, with no news of other transactions. As for auxiliary coinage, the situation was also very calm. Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly

Miscellaneous Notes on Medical and Pharmaceutical Supplements 174

— Ji Jilin

I recently read Mr. Wang Qizhang's masterpiece, "An Observation on the Statistics of Medical and Pharmaceutical Supplements in Local Newspapers," published in this publication. It is known that there are as many as sixteen kinds of regular medical and pharmaceutical publications in local newspapers, in addition to old medicine, which is quite a spectacle. My medical colleagues are enthusiastic about promoting medical and health knowledge. The crisis of our nation has reached its extreme. We are living in deep water and fire. Our lives are as fragile as a thread. The oppression of politics and economy is self-evident. Even population pressure is a serious problem. The cause of population pressure is often attributed to natural and man-made disasters. In fact, natural and man-made disasters are not insurmountable. However, due to the underdevelopment of medical and pharmaceutical undertakings, the lack of active health construction, and the lack of popularization of scientific medical knowledge, people die in droves and await death helplessly. Therefore, if we want to save the nation from danger, we should fight and struggle to find a way out from the oppression of politics and economy. The medical and health undertakings, which are closely related to the population problem, are also urgent tasks that cannot be ignored. There are many ways to study medicine and health, but it is most important to make the public understand the importance of medicine and health, so that they can generate power from faith. Therefore, written publicity is a necessary way. This is what my colleagues in the industry have to contribute to society in their spare time. Moreover, the current medical situation in our country is very complicated. There is new medicine based on science, and there is also mysterious and false old medicine. The advantages and disadvantages of the old and new coexist in society. The general public is confused and has no correct understanding. Even those in power in the temple are ambiguous and do not know what to do. They know the value of science, but also believe in the fallacies of old medicine. What could be more contradictory? Therefore, my colleagues in the industry, in order to make the society recognize the value of scientific new medicine and correct the conservative concepts of the public, must also promote medical and health knowledge. In recent years, social views have gradually changed. The contribution of publicity cannot be denied. However, if we observe with a strict eye, we will know that among the medical and pharmaceutical texts promoted in various newspapers today, there are many that have pure purposes and accurate arguments, but there are also those that are questionable. I, as a writer, embrace the meaning of Spring and Autumn criticism of the wise, and I cannot help but speak out about what I think is dangerous. For example, in the "Correspondence and Asking for Medical Advice" column of a certain medical publication, whether the drugs introduced in the answers are suitable for the patient is questionable. Moreover, most of the drugs are products of foreign merchants, and they are discarded like worn-out shoes for Chinese-made drugs with the same efficacy, and they are unwilling to introduce them. This makes our country's leak bigger and bigger, and we are willing to be the vanguard of foreign drugs. How can my medical colleagues not see this? Others, such as a certain medical publication, claim that certain dangerous diseases can only be cured by seeking treatment at a certain hospital or a certain doctor (in fact, the editor of the publication) to turn danger into safety. Academic attainments have their own depths, but to exaggerate one's own treatment achievements or to exaggerate words in order to attract patients is like a merchant. Its means are very despicable, and its intentions are even more questionable. How will the society regard our new doctors? May I ask if anyone will pay attention to the publicity of medical texts in the future? I dare to advise my colleagues in the industry that the purpose of publicizing medical and health knowledge must be pure, and the concept must not be for oneself, so that we can be righteous and speak loudly. Those who have knowledge will have firm faith. The promotion of medical and health undertakings will be rapid. Otherwise, one horse will harm the group, and other good publications will also be despised and perish together. A glimmer of dawn in the new medical community will be extinguished. Obstructing the development of new medicine and the survival of the nation is truly unbearable to say.

Beer Barrel and Seesaw 175

— Yue Qi

—One of the Medical Stories—

Various diagnostic methods for determining the symptoms of the lungs are now very complete; and "percussion" and "auscultation" are the most common and basic methods. Percussion is tapping the chest with fingers, and auscultation is listening to the chest with a stethoscope. Both use the doctor's sensitive hearing to distinguish the symptoms of the lungs from outside the skin. But the origin of these two diagnostic methods is quite an interesting story.

The birthplace of percussion was in the yard of a small inn in Graz, Austria, in the mid-18th century. The name of this small inn was Zum Swartzen Mohren, which means "marked by a Moorish black woman." The innkeeper's name was Auentruger, and his son's name was Leopold. He was born on November 19, 1722. After Leopold grew up, he helped his father manage the store. This inn also sold beer: the beer was stored in wooden barrels, and when it was needed, the wine would flow out as long as the plug on the side of the barrel was pulled out. Knowing how much wine was left in the barrel was very important economically. The barrel was made of wood, so how could people see the wine inside? But the young Leopold learned a method from his father, which, although not very accurate, was very simple. He stood the wine barrel firmly and tapped the side of the barrel with his palm from top to bottom. At the top, because there was only air and no wine inside, the tone was low: when he tapped to the place where there was wine inside, the tone suddenly became much higher.

Later, Leopold volunteered to study medicine, studied at the University of Vienna, and achieved good results; after practicing medicine, his reputation became increasingly prominent, and the king hired him as a royal physician. One day, one of his patients died. At that time, the practice of dissecting corpses had begun to prevail; he dissected the patient's corpse and found a liquid—pus—stored in the chest: this was a symptom he had not expected. So he thought to himself: why didn't he think that the patient's chest contained liquid when the patient was still alive? What method can be used to investigate whether there is liquid in the patient's chest? Suddenly, the scene of his father tapping the wine barrel with his hand appeared in his mind. The chest storing liquid is similar to a wooden barrel containing wine. The opaque skin is like the barrel wall; inside there is air at the top and liquid at the bottom. He decided to try it. From then on, whenever a patient called him to diagnose, he would gently tap his chest with his fingers and listen to the sound. This method was actually effective. By this method, he could find the liquid in the patient's chest, and occasionally find the consolidation of pulmonary tuberculosis and pneumonia. He called this method Percussicn, which means "percussion," and published an article in 1761 with the title of new invention.

Before that, no one had thought of "listening" to the sounds caused by air entering and leaving the lungs, or the sounds made by the heart pumping. This was invented unintentionally by another doctor in 1814.

One day, a French doctor named Rene Theophile Hjaeintbe Laemec was walking near the Nick Hospital in Paris. He was thin and frail, but he was the busiest and most fashionable doctor in Paris. The hospital was full of soldiers from the army. Most of them died of pulmonary tuberculosis. This kind doctor walked and thought: If there was a way to diagnose this disease early, the treatment would definitely be much easier. He inadvertently saw a group of children playing seesaw. They were not playing the usual seesaw game, but using the seesaw to "send telegrams." One put his ear to one end of the board to listen, and the other scratched the other end of the board with a needle; they still used their own "code" to scratch and listen, so as to transmit messages. The clever Laennec was suddenly inspired: If he used a wooden tube to press against his chest to listen, he might be able to hear the sound. He tried it, and there was indeed a sound. He recorded the various sounds he heard from the chests of various patients and compared the meanings of the various sounds from the corpse dissection, and he was actually successful. He was the founder of the stethoscope; his bronze statue still stands in the market square of Buimper.

The Consultation Fee for the Last Illness 176

— Song Guobin

The so-called "last illness" is the last illness in a person's life. In other words, it is the illness that sends them to their death. The last illness is something that everyone must go through, and it is also something that every doctor will inevitably encounter in the process of treating a certain number of patients. However, patients' families often take advantage of the patient's death to avoid paying the consultation fee. If the doctor tries to recover it, the patient's family will accuse the doctor of manslaughter and sue the doctor in court. Eight or nine out of ten medical disputes arise from recovering the consultation fee for the last illness. Therefore, the consultation fee for the last illness has become the most important issue for discussion between doctors and patients! Please discuss it in detail:

The consultation fee is a kind of compensation for the doctor's hard work. Its acceptance and payment are absolutely unrelated to the good or bad outcome of the disease, because seeing a doctor is a contract, and both the doctor and the patient have their own obligations to fulfill. Seeing a doctor is the doctor's obligation, and paying the consultation fee is the patient's family's obligation. If one party fails to fulfill their obligation, this clearly breaks the establishment of the contract. What is the definition of seeing a doctor? It is to sincerely and wholeheartedly relieve the patient's pain and do everything possible in terms of treatment. However, when encountering incurable diseases, bad outcomes occur, which no one can be responsible for. There is no such thing as a magical doctor who guarantees a cure in the world, and there is no such thing as a profession that works without pay. Can a small amount of consultation fee be considered the price of a patient's life? Nowadays, people in society often misunderstand this point and think that once they pay the consultation fee, they hope that the doctor will guarantee a cure. If the patient dies, they all think that it is due to the doctor's failure and not the disease, and use this as an excuse to avoid paying the consultation fee. Isn't this fundamentally wrong?

Since the definitions of consultation fee and seeing a doctor are as described above, then the consultation fee for the last illness should undoubtedly be paid. In Western countries, there are strict legal provisions for this consultation fee for the last illness. For example, Article 1201 of the French Civil Code states in essence:

"No matter what the outcome of the patient is, the patient's family or the deceased's heirs must pay the consultation fee for the last illness. Even if the patient's family goes bankrupt or sells their property, the doctor has the right to be paid first."

What should be noted in this law is the phrase "no matter what the outcome of the patient is," because no one can avoid death, and doctors cannot avoid treating the last illness. The meaning of this sentence is to prevent the patient's family from using the good or bad outcome of the disease as the standard for whether or not to pay the consultation fee. As for still having to repay even if bankrupt, this undoubtedly fears that the patient's family does not know that the consultation fee must be paid, and also prevents the patient's family from delaying or making excuses by saying that their income is insufficient or that they have gone bankrupt. From this point of view, the consultation fee is a kind of debt that the patient's family owes to the doctor, and the doctor is in the position of a prior creditor to the patient's family who has not paid the consultation fee! The legal knowledge of our people is shallower than that of advanced Western countries, and they do not know that paying the consultation fee is the patient's family's obligation. Our country's laws are also inevitably incomplete, so I have specially raised the issue of the consultation fee for the last illness for discussion in order to be selected by the legislators. This is also a way to protect the medical profession and reduce disputes between doctors and patients!

Common Sense of Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene 177

— Tang Renjin

(50) Eye Diseases Caused by Diabetes (Continued)

Diabetes, also known as consumption disease. Our country has known about it for a long time in the past. According to historical records, Sima Xiangru also suffered from it. The reason why old doctors named it consumption disease is that patients need to drink a lot of water due to the excessive amount of sugar in their blood, so that the sugar can be excreted by the kidneys. Because of this, patients often feel thirsty, and because a large amount of glucose cannot be used by the body and is excreted, the body's nutrition is affected and they gradually become thin. This is completely based on the symptoms of the disease. Pathologically speaking, the real cause of diabetes is the lesion of the Langerhans islands in the pancreas, resulting in the lack of secretions of the Langerhans islands (insulin) in the body. The function of insulin is to make liver sugar into glucose and to analyze and burn glucose to generate heat and energy. Once insulin is lacking, sugar in the blood cannot be burned and accumulates in the blood. Because blood has to maintain its inherent composition, it must excrete the increased sugar through the kidneys, otherwise hyperglycemia will occur. The symptoms of diabetes are roughly: polyuria, gluttony, easy hunger, often need to drink a lot of water due to thirst, people gradually become thin and feel exhausted. Most of the patients are upper-class people who often eat refined foods and exercise less. This disease does have a hereditary relationship. In addition, obesity and gout can also cause it. The causes of obesity and gout are all due to eating too much food rich in protein and fat, and the person is less active. These people often feel comfortable in life, and it is difficult to feel polyuria, gluttony, easy hunger, thirst, and drinking a lot, but because of good nutrition, they do not lose weight, so they often suffer from the disease for a long time without realizing it. Most of them are found only after physical examination and urine examination. If it is a mild disease, it does not matter much, but if it is severe, it may cause diabetic coma (Kema Diabeticum) and may be life-threatening. Therefore, if diabetes can be detected early, and attention is paid to diet, there is no danger to life. Now, in addition to the sugar content in urine that is generally known, the changes in the visual organs caused by diabetes can also be used as an aid to early diagnosis. Common visual organ lesions are oculomotor nerve palsy, eye rigidity, which can cause needle vision or have regulation, paralysis and bismuth nerve atrophy, resulting in weakened vision, double vision or blindness. Sometimes it can cause cataracts, called diabetic cataracts (Katarakta Diabetika), which cause visual impairment and blindness. The most important thing in early diagnosis is indeed diabetic retinitis (Retinitfs Diabetica). The main subjective aspect of this disease is initially only weakened vision, or slight visual impairment, or even no feeling at all. It must be examined by a specialist ophthalmologist to see the retina, there are bright white spots, very similar to proteinuria retinitis, often mistaken for kidney inflammation proteinuria caused by, in fact, it is due to the relationship of diabetes. From this, we can know that fundus examination can not only diagnose eye diseases, but also can detect changes in the eyes caused by internal diseases. Generally, people think that eye diseases are local diseases and do not pay attention to them. In fact, many eye diseases have a close relationship with internal diseases. For example, diabetes mentioned today, in addition, kidney inflammation, leukemia (Leukamie), etc., can be diagnosed accurately through fundus examination in the early stage.

Popular Lectures on Modern Venereology (4) 178

— Chen Shengbai (Compiled and Narrated) Yin Muqiang (Proofread)

Other symptoms manifest as changes in toxicity.

Nail disorders such as onychitis, paronychia.

Periosteum and bone disorders such as periostitis, osteitis, and osteomyelitis.

Joint and muscle disorders such as syphilitic arthritis, myositis.

Circulatory system disorders such as myocarditis, arteritis, phlebitis.

Nervous system disorders such as meningitis, spinal leptomeningitis and spinal cord gumma, and the aforementioned spinal cord tuberculosis, paralytic dementia.

Visual and auditory organ disorders such as interstitial keratitis, iritis, cyclitis, optic neuritis, and diseases of the external ear, middle ear, and inner ear, etc.

Urogenital disorders such as kidney disease and testicular disease.

Furthermore, diseases of various internal organs such as hepatitis, liver atrophy, lungs, pancreas, and spleen. The insidious harm and bizarre transformations are truly beyond description. What is described here is only a brief overview. As for the above diseases, each has its own characteristics. I deeply fear generating unnecessary details and dazzling the senses, so they are also omitted.

Furthermore, it is necessary to describe the symptoms of congenital syphilis. According to congenital syphilitic fetuses, they often die in utero from damage caused by syphilitic pathogens and are aborted, or are born prematurely with various syphilitic lesions. Therefore, the nutrition and development of the fetus are very poor, and the skin is scaly, white, dry, or prematurely dirty, yellowish-white, and full of wrinkles, resembling an old man. As for the invasion of various organs, the infiltration of the skin can cause blisters on the palms and soles, i.e., pemphigus-like syphilitic rash. Also, the fissures in the infiltrated area around the mouth leave radiating scars, i.e., the so-called Parrot's furrows. In mucosal lesions, rhinitis can obstruct breathing and make breastfeeding difficult, or destroy nasal cartilage and bone, leading to a sunken nasal bridge (saddle nose – shaped like a saddle). Furthermore, hair loss, or inflammation of the bones and periosteum of the limbs, can present as a state of pseudo-paralysis, i.e., Parrot's pseudo-paralysis. As for the nervous system, encephalitis, meningitis, idiocy, epilepsy, etc., may occur in abundance. There is also the so-called Hutchinson's triad, which is a unique symptom of late-onset congenital syphilis, namely (1) malformed permanent teeth with short, narrow, and thin upper incisors, with a semi-lunar notch on the lower edge; (2) keratitis of the eye; and (3) ear disorders. Syphilis symptoms are like this. Clear-eyed people should be able to imagine the magnitude of its harm.

Chapter 6: The Value and Recent Progress of Syphilis Diagnosis

After contracting syphilis, it not only invades oneself and close relatives, but also harms future generations without end. It goes without saying that syphilis must be thoroughly treated. However, we already know that the changes in this disease are so numerous that they crown all diseases. Therefore, the diagnosis of this disease requires detailed investigation to fully understand its capabilities. This is something that those who hope to fundamentally eliminate syphilis must know.

Before the discovery of 606, the main symptom of syphilis was skin rash. Therefore, opinions... After the discovery of 606, skin symptoms decreased significantly. There are often cases where no skin rash appears after the first stage. This is especially true for those in large cities who have some basic knowledge of venereal diseases. However, who knows if the symptoms on the surface have subsided, but the toxicity still exists? Therefore, even doctors can know the general idea based on the patient's past history and current symptoms. Even if the patient has undergone treatment and the symptoms have lessened, a thorough diagnosis is still necessary. Do not neglect it.

The diagnostic methods include (1) bacteriological examination – to detect the presence or absence of the pathogenic bacteria of this disease; (2) histological observation – to examine the changes in tissues and determine whether they are syphilitic; (3) optical fluoroscopy – to examine lesions in deep organs. Furthermore, it is necessary to perform

(4) Serological examination

(A) Complement fixation reaction, i.e., Wassermann reaction

(B) Turbidity reaction, including

a. Kahn test

b. Sachs-Georgi test

c. Meinicke test, etc.

The positive rate of serum reactions is highest in the secondary stage, followed by the tertiary and quaternary stages, and then the primary stage.

(5) Cerebrospinal fluid examination

(A) Wassermann reaction

(B) Cell count

(C) Protein reaction

(D) Colloid reaction, etc.

Medical Pain Relief (18) 179

— Li Xing

Furuncles, Carbuncles, Cellulitis, Abscesses

There are several painful skin and flesh ailments, sometimes very dangerous. What patients want is pain relief, and doctors should also relieve patients' pain, reducing pain where possible and eliminating danger where possible. Although patients want pain relief, they must also consider the safety of their lives.

Furuncles are localized skin inflammation, mostly healing gradually after suppuration. The cause is staphylococcus bacteria growing in hair follicles or skin sebaceous glands. Some people have furuncles all year round, appearing one after another, mostly due to impaired kidney excretion, diabetes, or impaired sugar metabolism in the body.

Furuncles are usually not very large, and the pain is limited, mostly without danger. At the beginning of a furuncle, using saturated magnesium sulfate solution to soak a cloth pad and applying hot and cold compresses can significantly benefit pain relief and swelling reduction. Doing this several times a day may hopefully resolve the furuncle. It is also acceptable to apply pain-relieving ointment or pain-relieving lotion. There are two more things to pay attention to regarding furuncles, namely: (1) be sure to protect the furuncle from injury, as injury can enlarge the furuncle and allow bacteria to enter the blood, causing danger. (2) When the furuncle is ripe and contains pus, it must be cut open to release the pus. Do not be afraid of temporary minor pain. If the pus is not released, the pus in the furuncle is easily absorbed by the blood and transported to other parts of the body, which can cause sores and inflammation, and if transported to the kidneys, it can cause nephritis. Cutting open a furuncle to release pus is also a pain-relieving method. Without cutting, the furuncle is tense and painful; after cutting, the tension disappears and the pain stops naturally.

Carbuncles are a type of gangrene in the skin and flesh, due to localized invasion of pus-producing staphylococcus bacteria. Patients are mostly those with low physical resistance. Those with kidney disease and diabetes are more prone to carbuncles. Carbuncles initially become hard and painful, with the skin on the carbuncle turning red and gray, and the swelling gradually expanding to the size of a rice bowl is not uncommon. The most common sites for furuncles are the neck, back, shoulders, and buttocks, because these areas have lower tissue resistance.

Carbuncles on the face are commonly called "boils." Most people also know that boils are dangerous. As for why boils are dangerous, they cannot explain why, but they know that some people die from boils. We know that the blood flow in the face is very abundant, and part of the blood return in the face first goes to the base of the brain through the veins and then returns to the heart. Blood clots often form from bacteria in the veins of the carbuncle, causing inflammation to spread to the large veins at the base of the brain. If the large veins at the base of the brain are invaded by bacteria and become purulent, the disease cannot be cured. Once there are venous blood clots, toxic bacteria can easily enter the blood. Bacterial invasion of the blood is also a difficult disease to cure. Bacterial invasion of the large veins at the base of the brain is a particular danger of facial carbuncles (boils). Bacterial invasion of the blood is a danger that can be caused by any carbuncle.

Since carbuncles are so dangerous, the treatment should be based on two goals: first, to relieve pain. Doctors should always relieve patients' pain within possible limits. Pain relief should use local methods and not systemic methods. Note that injecting anesthetics and taking pain-relieving pills are systemic methods. We know that carbuncles are a very dangerous disease with a very high mortality rate, so the patient's complete physical resistance should be preserved. Anesthetics and pain-relieving pills often reduce physical resistance. In the face of a dangerous disease, a fraction of resistance is of great importance to life and death. Do not recklessly seek temporary pain relief and destroy the chance of survival.

Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (55) 180

— Hu Jiayan

In the treatment of pneumothorax, in addition to the patient needing absolute rest, all physical examination work must be reduced as much as possible; the use of anesthetics is also necessary, but most are not very effective. Relieving dyspnea is the most important task, and the most important aspect of this is the aspiration of air from the chest cavity! This is not a very easy operation, and doctors should proceed with caution. If there is excessive effusion, perform a thoracentesis; for pyopneumothorax, repeated thoracentesis should be performed, or ordinary surgical drainage for empyema can also be used, but attention should be paid to tuberculosis patients.

Section 4: Digestive Tract

Regarding complications of the digestive tract, intestinal tuberculosis is the most important! The number of its sufferers is truly staggering; according to pathologists' reports, in the overall population of tuberculosis patients, almost more than 50% are also suffering from intestinal tuberculosis. It is found after severe open tuberculosis: not to mention exudative types, even proliferative ulcerative types are the same. Its occurrence is mostly caused by the sputum coughed up by pulmonary tuberculosis patients being swallowed from the throat and reaching the intestines; the tuberculosis bacteria in the sputum are of course its medium! In addition, primary intestinal tuberculosis is also possible; such as the ingestion of tuberculous milk, uncooked tuberculous animal meat, and the careless use of utensils by tuberculosis patients are all very obvious causes: this situation has already been briefly mentioned in the "Foodborne Transmission" section of Chapter 2 of this book; I think readers can probably still recall it.

Page 15

Chunqiu (Annals)

Snippets 181

— (Shen Shou Ruo)

Nowadays, all kinds of writing instruments are truly improving day by day, and the manufacturing is becoming more and more refined. However, I think this is not a good phenomenon in terms of culture: because although the writing instruments are good, the production of articles has not made new progress so far. Then, what's the use of merely holding a "silver-like wax gun head"!

When a car is on the way and the engine malfunctions, stopping its progress, it is called "breaking down": when a ship is sailing on the waterway and the engine breaks down, unable to move forward, it is called "inserting candles". I think that reversing the two terms (this so-called term is my arbitrary decision) would be more correct, but the general public insists on misidentifying them to the end, I don't know why? Therefore, all things in society that subvert right and wrong can be viewed in this way.

Literacy Movement 182

— Wei Jing

I have a friend who is in the education field, and he is very dedicated to the newly emerging literacy movement. Yesterday I met him again and asked him how effective his efforts were in persuading illiterate people to learn to read. He shook his head, sighed, and said, "Difficult!"

He said, "In my neighbor's house, an old nanny, about thirty years old, is employed. I thought it was very important to have her learn some words, so I taught her three words every day after my classes, along with her work breaks. I thought that in this way, after a year, she could recognize about a thousand words."

"I taught her so seriously, and she read very seriously too. But after a week, the old nanny refused me for no reason. Afterwards, I learned that her mistress said that the old nanny was getting too close to me and wanted to stop her business."

"At the same time, I also taught the rickshaw puller across the street every day. I also planned to teach him to recognize a thousand words in a year. Who knew that his master was a businessman who ate gold and had not even finished three years of schooling, and was afraid that the rickshaw puller would know too many words, which would undermine his glory, so he forced the rickshaw puller to stop learning by ridiculing and threatening him."

"In a leather craftsman's stall in the alley, there were two apprentices, both of whom had never read a book in their lives, so I thought I would teach them three words each every day. After teaching them for three days, they stopped reading. When asked for the reason, they said that time is more precious than anything else to craftsmen. Although reading three words every day doesn't seem to take much time, if you count it for a quarter of an hour every day, you would have to do a lot less work for a month. Craftsmen would starve if they stopped working, so how could they have time to learn to read?"

"Also, there was a maid in a wealthy family in the alley. I had only taught her to recognize six words, and she was punished by her mistress by being starved for a day." He said dejectedly, "In this day and age, it is still very difficult to promote the literacy movement."

But in the end, he still said very firmly, "No matter what, I will still work hard!"

A Record of a Giant Ship Model 183

— Zhang Huang

At the intersection of Jiangxi Road and Fuzhou Road, there is the Italian Postal Shipping Company. In its street-facing glass window, a postal ship model is displayed, about ten feet in length, with realistic construction and exquisite craftsmanship, truly a concrete and miniature representation. Those who catch a glimpse of it for the first time have their minds wander to the land of water and clouds, yearn for the scenery of foreign countries, and seem to have placed themselves in the realm of extreme material enjoyment, unable to contain the joy of returning home, and often marvel at its perfect craftsmanship, lingering and looking around, unable to leave. Connoisseurs say: "The creation of this model is entirely based on the original ship, and its ability to sail is as desired; the cost has reached twenty thousand gold yuan." Westerners spare no effort and expense in their business promotion, to this extent! Today, the Italians exclusively hold the hegemony of Eurasian water transport, can it be without reason?

Looking back at our country, shipping and transportation are left to foreigners to overstep their boundaries without competition, and those sailing to foreign oceans do not even have a single ship. Even the small achievements that have been made are those who compete for profit and engage in infighting, and will not stop until they are completely destroyed. As for the new ships purchased with embezzled funds by those who are greedy and boast to the people, examining their usefulness, I wonder if they can surpass this postal ship model in any way? It's just that no one has compared them!

Alas! This is the shame of our people!

Little Western Paradise 186

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 14: A Westerner Talks About Construction, Not Without Regret; A Poor Scholar Yearns for Love

You Rong picked up the cartoon and looked at it. It depicted a highway with a large Pigsy wielding a large nail rake, digging the road forward. In front of the road was dense undergrowth, but in the opened-up highway area, there were people coming and going, all with high noses, occasionally mixed with a few wearing cloth shoes. The people coming each carried an empty pocket, with the one in the front holding a flag that read "Go to Northwest China." The people going, on the other hand, were different. Each person's pocket was swollen like a toad's belly. There was the letter "F" on the pocket. The person in front raised his thumb, and two curved lines came out of his mouth, with words written in the lines: "The impression is very good, construction is progressing." You Rong looked at it, put it down, and clapped his hands and laughed: "The meaning is very good. But I suspect you are reversing the car, opposing the construction of the highway." Zhiqian laughed: "You are studying politics, and I am acting as a pro-people official, you might as well come and solve this problem. The facts are laid out here. Whether transportation is convenient or not, in China, the proportion of foreign economic aggression becomes formal. Now, in Xi'an city, buying a bottle of beer costs more than one yuan, and a bottle of brandy costs twelve or thirteen yuan. Of course, the middle class doesn't dare to ask about it. In the future, when the train reaches outside the North Gate of Xi'an, beer can be sold for four or five mao, and brandy can also be sold for four or five yuan, and more people will drink it. The top-quality imported goods, before the train reached Tongguan and the car could not reach Xi'an, could only be bought in a few stores in Xi'an city. Since the train has reached Tongguan and the highway has reached Xi'an, this has undergone a great change. Several three-story foreign-style buildings have been built in Nan Yuan Men, all selling foreign goods. The foreign goods that can be bought in Kaifeng and Zhengzhou can also be bought slowly here." (235)

A Record of the Lingering Fragrance 187

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shou Ou

Just because of this exchange, the Empress Dowager's appearance also changed greatly. She seemed to have lost twenty years of age all at once, as if she had returned to her youth. Her spirit was more lively than those of us young people, and her every word and action was so light and quick that it was almost indescribable. What was the reason for this? Actually, there was no particular reason, only that in the recent days, all the political affairs in the court had been going very smoothly, without anything that could make her angry or sad, and today was particularly free, without any major matters that she had to take care of herself, so she was especially happy. Really, her good complexion today would definitely make it very suitable to wear the pair of jade earrings and the pair of white jade bracelets offered by Zhang Zhidong. However, although I thought of this, the Empress Dowager herself did not express it, perhaps because she didn't think of it at that moment.

"Today, we must think of a more interesting way to play...! Let's go to Kunming Lake!" Her lively mood could no longer allow her to sit still, so she decided to go out and play, first expressing to us: "With such good weather, we must have a good time for most of the day: isn't it very interesting to be on the water? Even our lunch must be ordered to be brought to the boat, otherwise we won't be able to enjoy ourselves!"

Of course, we were all happy to hear this and eagerly obeyed the order. Before setting off, the eight of us lady officials specially gathered quietly and held a five-minute meeting. (325)
